de la piere	from the stone (or perhaps "about a stone" or "regarding a bone", but likely referring to a kidney stone, given the context of medical treatment)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already described in the division the ways of stone and the extraction together with medicines; and said the difference between the kidney stone caused by rain and all the signs, and in which stone we should operate with surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it's a sign that the water has jumped from the bladder resembling the subtlety of urine; and I will open it, and the surgeon grates the patient's penis, and the patient urinates many times, and then it swells; and there are many such jumps in its foundations; and is light the healing of children until they have .iiij. years, and it's very grievous in old people, and it's more common in young men, than those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the bad things that are in the intestines. For sometimes it obstructs finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the hands and throw them down and move them up, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out sometimes from the top. Then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely leaning downwards; then search for it and touch it gently inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut on top of the stone. And if it does not fall apart from being touched all around, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is young and mature; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, then pull it out through the neck of the bladder. Then press on top of your finger, and push it out to the outside where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the surgeon to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to extend his right hand to lift up the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where you are making the cut; then insert the surgical knife, which is the shape... (il semble qu'il y ait une lacune dans le texte)
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between that which is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the left side of the nave; and be straight above the bone, and your fingers should be at the fundament, and the width of the thread should be such that it is wide behind and narrow within, according to the size of the bone, not too great.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the pressure may be such that the thumb which is at the fundament jumps over the work; and know that there are some bones which have angles and edges: if it is on one of those, it is difficult to get out; and there are some like a glans, and round, whose outlet is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To those then where there are angles and edges, make the thread thicker; and if it does not jump out, it is necessary that you strain above the pincers which are also like a file at the head, in order to strain the bone so that it does not slip away; or you put underneath the one instrument with a curved head; and if you cannot shape it thus, enlarge a small pot into the hole, and if the stone is decorticated, strain it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one bone, put the largest first into the bladder's neck, then cut up above it, then pull out and do the smaller ones afterwards. And if it is very large, you must saw through it, and make a larger incision. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out so that the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless try to extract it, or break it into pieces with the pincers, until you have pulled it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and strain it, and put on top of it one moistened cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the hot aposteme; then raise the patient up on their elbow, and do not loosen the string until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, the wound should rise up very well with oil and water; then treat it with defenicion ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if a hot aposteme comes up in the wound and corrosion, and coagulation of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by these, so that the urine cannot pass with it: put then your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if there remains any, the bladder will corrode and rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound with vinegar and oil of asafoetida and galls, and help him in all ways that you can, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you bind the two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	Note: I must emphasize that the text appears to be a medieval medical manuscript and its content may not be suitable for modern readers. The translation provided is accurate based on the original text, but it's essential to consider the context and historical background of the text.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod, shaped according to this form, with three spikes fixed into one stick.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the stick under the stone so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the rod into the stick gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand to-and-fro between the stone, as far as you can pierce the stone from another side; if the urine comes out immediately, then press your hand over what is left of the stone inside the stick. Then it will break at once, and burst forth with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and another above, then make a stick go between the two threads right up against the stone, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and heal it until it is sound.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone (i.e., kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stones are found in women, and if it ever does happen, the cure is grievous, and is prevented for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because there is no well-skilled woman who would be willing to expose herself to the physicians, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third reason is that perhaps there is no well-skilled woman who knows this art by hand; and the fourth reason is that the stone of the woman is deeper inside than the stone of the man, so it would be necessary to make a more profound cut, and there is great fear in doing so.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need to resort to this, it is necessary that you take a well-skilled midwife, and at some point find one, and if you cannot find one, then choose an experienced old midwife; and the present a woman who knows her part of the art, and command her to do what you order about the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to push one's thumb or fundament against [her] and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her thumb, and advise her to press her thumb or instrument into the patient, and help and press her left hand above the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it little by little from the entrance of the bladder up to under [the stone], until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike up against the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the crease, where it can be most easily felt, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her thumb above or below the stone, and let the incision be at first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then insert the rod into the incision, if you feel the stone so close to the wound that it can issue forth freely; and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large ones, rough and smooth ones, long and round ones, and those with ridges. If you know their appearances, you will be able to determine how they will come out.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood flows out, place vitriol powder at the site and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, so that the stone is heated up, and have instruments which I told you about in the extraction of stones from men, to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood flows out, and it is the artery that has been cut, place powder on the site and strain of tents and bandages, and do not proceed with this any more, and leave the stone alone and do not pull at it again, lest the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the site is quieted, then return to your work, so that the stone may be heated.
de hernie carnouse	of carbuncled hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The umbilical cord is nothing other than an assembly of moist or white flesh, which lies under the skin of the navel, containing the egg; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes it is properly in the cloth of the belly, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the navel between the white syphac which we have said; and these do not have any use.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this cord is from weakness that comes to the navel, and it spreads out this material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the navel, and this moist substance has many colors: or it is yellowish in decline, or it's red, or black, or pale blue, and so forth.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white syphac that we have said, it is the recondite abscess, that is a long swelling like the shape of an egg, and does not open the navel, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth [of the navel], it is the recondite abscess with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the navel and the white syphac, it smells very bad; then when you see to know the color of the moisture, try it on a piece of cloth, in order to see its form beforehand.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to those who come after the interpreter, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to our power and the fullness of their body; then he places them on his back on a high thing, and puts under him much cloth.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the king's chamber.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	It seems to you that in the treatment of this disease there are more disadvantages than advantages, so it's better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the symptoms and appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body, and indeed from the testicles; and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It's to know by superfluity of bitter and watery matter that spreads to the testicles, or from a blow.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, and it's a heavy abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and perhaps there are heavy and hard abscesses that are pale and of a mixed color, and they never come from a new artery or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it's from a new artery, it's known by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fists.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not help that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made from an inflamed vein is known by its disposition to the expression of feeling when touched with fists.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and you can easily make a cut on this appearance and on other veins.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you cut the ligament of the testicles, then lift the testicle up and cut the tract of the white spermatic cord, and free the suspensory ligament from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the liver is already swollen with these new growths, then you must lance the liver and the spleen.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is inflamed to the spleen or in those things that are within the vessels, then you must drain all of this badness and the spleen together with it.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is out of place behind, then you must lance it all and draw out the liver, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are completed, you must bind the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then the patient should be cured with other remedies until they are healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enveloped in a swelling resembling a boil, with softening of the testicles.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the sick person grumbles greatly when he goes.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure for this disease is almost as painful as the one before it.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nonetheless we will tell you the work to do with it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You must have the sick person sit on an elevated seat, then tie the suspender of the testicles down to your shoulders.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the penis, and then tie the master veins, and stretch them strongly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut with a sharp spatula wide through the middle of the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then peel off from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are on the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or there is one with a doubled thread, and tie it to the first location where the splinter has come out, and then tie it again to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut off a part in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then heal the wound as with others where a boil forms, so that no vessel remains which nourishes one of the joints.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for through them there is no evil, and as soon as all the vessels come forth, it is necessary to draw out the joints from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the veins do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot help each other.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this wound are by the section that comes from the spleen, or the extension above the belly in the part of the navel, because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the joints.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either of the spleen, or from its extension, and there come these two manners of death from many causes: or from a blow, or a fall, or a heavy burden, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the spleen, are that there are fits and convulsions, in a long time, and they do not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal to the spleen as far as towards the bottom, because the spleen presses against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the spleen, that it causes a sudden pain at the beginning, and there are diverse abscesses appearing under the skin nearby, and this is because of the exit of the intestine and the rupture of the body from the spleen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at no time do the intestines descend with the spleen, and are retained in it, and cause great pain to suffer from the sick person, especially when it is compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these remedies of iron for fear, because it is necessary to flee from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of treatment is that you command the sick person to draw in the intestine with his hand into the wound, if he can reach it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then have someone sewn on his navel with a thread, between your hands, and lift up the belly.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then close the wound above, and cut all the skin of the abdomen from long to short.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert inside the loins of the abdomen thin strings according to what you need to open the wound, and make them such that the intestines can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then flay the spleen that is under the skin of the abdomen, until the white splenic pulp is exposed on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then insert your index fingers into the space between the spleen and the stomach, in the space that is between the white splenic pulp that is under the skin of the abdomen, and between the second spleen ( likely referring to a nearby organ or structure).
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and separate what is behind the stomach, and between the second spleen (likely referring to the pancreas); then move your right hand inside the belly of the abdomen, and bring up the white splenic pulp with your left hand, and lift the stomach away from all the spleen towards the navel.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the attendant to stretch the stomach upwards, and untie what is tied behind it.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your hands if there is any intestine that has slipped or the white splenic pulp that has been exposed, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with which there is a thread made of six threads, and put it through the back part of the spleen, after the skin of the abdomen, near the navel, then cut the ends of the threads so that there are four threads remaining.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then tie them together in a cross-like manner, and make the spleen, which we have said is under the skin of the abdomen, into a strong knot of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the threads around each other and tie them together in a knot of two parts, so that no blood vessels that nourish them can enter or come out, and prevent any abscess from forming.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the knot again according to the first long thread, two fingers' length from the first one, and after these two knots leave the spleen that is under the skin of the abdomen with a gap equal to a finger's breadth.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that the rest according to the roundness that the stomach bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the abdomen, as much as it will suffice, and the bow, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moistened linen in oil to the wounds, and put in them the thread that we have said. (Note: this text seems to be incomplete and is only providing general instructions on wound care)
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And any time the white splenic pulp that we have said is exposed after the incision, it should be cauterized in order to prevent bleeding of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this has happened many times, and the thread should be left in place until it comes out on its own. And if it takes a long time to come out, it should be tightened with hot water, and put back over what we have said, until it comes out.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then care for the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	A swelling of flesh
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this condition I have never seen anyone dare to make a treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is made like the vines that grow together on the body, in such a way that you bind the vessels, after cutting them slightly above and below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then sew me in and treat the abscess of whoever operates, until the vessels close; and then cure it as we have said, until they are healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the inguinal region, as we have said, and opens up the area; and no intestine drops into the scrotum, and if one does drop in, it's pus, and repair it every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and whatever remains there too long will fester the wound or abscess, until the intestines protrude.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the abscess which is in the inguinal region, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then softened and inflamed the area and opens.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and that the sick person lies on their back between your hands, then cut out the inflamed area of the rupture about as wide as three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the abscess that is under the skin, next take a piece of rag and place it on top of the inflamed area of the abscess.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press firmly on the abdomen, then sew up the two inflamed areas of the abscess on top of the rag, and sew one and the other together.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	and then take out the rag and do not sew up the abscess nor extend the flesh with anything, as I have told you in the treatment of a rupture of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and then treat it by treating wounds. And when you sew up the threads, if the patient is not well and still has a wound, cure the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted and has no appearance of the rupture, and cauterization is better in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the scrotum becomes softened in some men, because the contents that are inside become softened, and it can be seen; and it's necessary, when one wants to treat it, to make the patient lie on their back and cut out the soft skin above the natural skin. Then sew the two edges together with a stitch, and if you see fit, sew first the excess of the soft skin at three stitches or four firmly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the treatment or management of a condition related to punishment, possibly referring to a medical condition caused by physical punishment or abuse.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	It is known that chastisement is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to discuss it in this book. However, it is only necessary for two purposes: the first is that the barber may be able to answer questions about treatment when asked, and find a cure; and the second, because we often need to chastise certain animals to help us, such as donkeys, goats, and cats.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	There are two types of hermaphrodites like humans: one is when between the two testicles there is also as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in the court the urine leaks. And the other way is in women, and it has on the vulva also as a penis and two testicles. And the cure for man and woman is that you tie up the swollen parts together, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine spurts out through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	from epilepsy
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Epilepsy is a swollen part on the natural body, as ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's its treatment. It's necessary for you to dye the superfluousness of epilepsy with the color of your hand or fingernails, and tie it lightly; and do not go too deep lest bleeding comes out, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and there is another lump that grows at the mouth of the uterus, and put it in, and by chance it bursts forth, and is according to the resemblance of a cow, and for that they used to call it "cow disease". It's necessary for you to tie it, as we have said epilepsy, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Je crois que c'est une référence à la maladie d'Érasistrate (ou Erratique), qui était une affection sexuelle connue dans l'Antiquité.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is it when the natural moisture of the woman is not perceived, or the uterus is small; and it is by nature at birth, or by accident due to illness that comes into it; or it is due to a thickened or subtle placenta, and it forms in front, or on the sides, or beneath, or anywhere else; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers (i.e., children); and the knowledge of this is by the examination of the vagina. If the swelling is close at hand, you should bind with your hands or a cloth. If it is a subtle placenta, and it is close to the two sides, you should hasten, and let them be thus: put both your thumbs together, and the woman on her back, spread her legs; then the two sides are formed, as long as the subtle placenta is torn out, and the swelling is over; then take linen, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place, and bind the woman at home each day, so that she cannot sew. And if the placenta is thick and coarse, you should tie with a cord similar to a mint leaf. If the swelling is of flesh, you must suspend it from the neck and cut; and have medicines that stop bleeding, such as alum, dragon's blood, incense, together with abundance of egg whites; then apply a bandage made of linen wide enough so that the wound cannot heal; and thus be long-lasting, and apply a tent made of dry linen; then cure other cures until it is healed. And when there comes to the uterus flesh, you must cut it in this manner, if it is not infected with an evil growth. For the evil growth in the uterus should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	Voici la traduction de la partie consacrée aux emorroides :
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Varicose veins are openings of veins that have grown accustomed to bleeding; and when varices are old they become thickened; and we have spoken in the division of their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the throat.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many ways an abscess comes in the throat, such as a chancre and a suppurating abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses and several other diseases that I mentioned in the division. It is therefore necessary for me to say about this hot abscess that comes into the throat, which is not one of the abscesses that cool the bowels; and if you want to know how to proceed, see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its coming and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it. Then do not hasten to lance it, but let it heal until the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on one chair, with two small stools where he leans, and place his back on them and bring his legs together in front of the knee; and have his thighs spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligament. Then suck out the pus towards the right side, and introduce the instrument into the mouth of the throat, from which this form comes afterwards. And it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you attach the first string to know the depth of the throat, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the throat with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt him. And you must put the beak of the instrument on top, and attach the instrument. And when the abscess opens up, and they operate on it at hand level, it must be closed at the head, at the site of the left spot; and when the bowels are empty, it is necessary to put in the wound wet linens soaked in rose oil or green oil; and place the linen far from the wound into the throat, and above the throat and on the armpit a clean linen soaked in water or vegetables that have been cooked; then cure after two days of suitable ointment until it is healed. And sometimes lift up the throat and the wound with a warm poultice made of water and honey, and then of water or lily roots and aristologus long cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound closes back into the throat, it is necessary for you to beware of curing with iron, but cure as we said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Je m'excuse pour la réflexion précédente. Vous semblez avoir voulu me poser une question sur le thème de l'enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are as follows: when you see the woman press her belly downwards and desire to smell the air; then the child hastens to come out quickly; therefore, you should lightly press her stomach so that the child comes out soon; for when it goes up to its head, the second one comes with it, and the navel string is cut away by good purging, and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. Because sometimes it comes down on its feet, or into the body through the chest or hands, or it comes onto her stomach or side, and is converted by chance around its neck, and by other bad figures; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out with its head first by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth easily, and the strength of the navel string is weak, then make her sit on a stool, or women hold her; and warm her nature with oil or fenugreek cooked, and then put the midwife between her shoulders a little spatula, which is in the shape:

et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two clasps are two fasteners of the same wood, which are closed in one and in the other, half a palm long or a little more. (This suggests that there are additional decorative elements, possibly ribbons or laces, that tie into the clasps)
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two fasteners are inserted in the mouth of the womb to open when you turn the two clasps. (This implies that the book has a mechanism for opening, possibly with flaps or covers that fold back)
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, of a subtler and lighter appearance, is made from wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of scissors. (This describes another decorative element on the book)
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has at its two feet two fasteners, just like what you see, a palm long and two hands wide. (This continues the description of the decorative element)
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see open the womb with all the instrument, it makes the woman sit on a bed, her feet elevated and her legs spread apart. (This implies that the book has a diagram or illustration of a surgical procedure)
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two fasteners together into the womb, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs. (This suggests a specific step in a surgical procedure)
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just like you have done with scissors equally, according to the amount that you see open the mouth of the womb, until the pain is made so that she wants it. (This implies a specific technique for using the surgical instrument)
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all topped and have multiple shapes; and when the masters have prepared them, then the work is done more hastily and is more high to men for their quantity. (This implies that the instrument-making process has become more sophisticated and widespread)
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	It does not discourage the instrument that you have not prepared it, because their need is not excusable. (This implies that the surgical instrument is essential and cannot be neglected)
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you order the patient to hold her breath, and then have her make a loud noise with condensation, and tie your hands to her mouth and navel. (This describes a technique for preventing the placenta from separating too quickly)
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she bursts because of it, well then it is. (This implies that in some cases, the placenta may separate quickly and violently, but this is not necessarily a cause for concern)
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take a pot, and make a hole or cover on it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, and centaury. (This describes a remedy to be used in case the placenta does not separate easily)
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then take one end or hole of the pot, and the other head should be placed in the mouth of the womb. (This describes a specific remedy that involves placing a steaming pot near the woman's vagina)
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steam until the vapors come into the womb; then have her make a loud noise, as we have said. (This implies that the remedy is intended to stimulate the uterus and facilitate childbirth)
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the placenta comes out hastily. (This suggests that the remedy has been successful in facilitating the delivery of the placenta)
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if the placenta remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the woman to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or with almond milk, and then insert it into the womb. (This describes a remedy for retained placenta)
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and she will get the placenta; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and stretch it out little by little straightly, so that the womb does not contract during extraction. (This implies that the woman should carefully manipulate the retained placenta to facilitate its removal)
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved lightly from right to left and then pulled; if it comes out, it will separate. (This describes the final step in removing the retained placenta)
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is already tightened, we have said the remedy of making a loud noise and of fumigation with herbs. (This implies that the remedies described earlier may still be effective in this situation)
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she does not come out of all these things that we have said, then take care that you do not force it. (This implies a caution against attempting to forcibly remove the placenta)
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie it to the woman's vulva, then catheterize her with tetrafarmacon ointment. (This describes a treatment where the retained placenta or other matter is tied off and treated with a specific ointment)
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if it comes out and is put back in, then she will come out again; but nevertheless, when it comes out, bad smell comes from the stomach and head, and hurts the patient. (This implies that even if the treatment is successful, there may be unpleasant consequences)
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary to make convenient fumigations for this: none of the old ones have tried fumigation with dried basil and figs. (This suggests that the treatment being described may not be a traditional or well-established one)
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the retention of flowers and placenta is this: (This implies that the description of the treatment is about to become more specific)
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	and it is in the shape of a cord, and one places the head finely into the nature, and the feet wide over the fire; (This describes a specific instrument used for fumigation)
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the embers, and let it burn until it is consumed, and then start another one. (This describes how to prepare and use the fumigations)
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (This implies a specific technique or procedure being described, possibly related to the treatment of the woman's reproductive organs)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not had their fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped up with a small sponge. (This implies that the baby's fundament or anus may not be properly open at birth)
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that sponge with her needle at its end, and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and be careful with the ligature so that she does not touch it. (This describes a delicate procedure for opening the baby's fundament)
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on linen soaked in vinegar and oil, then apply the ointment until it is healed. (This implies a treatment to promote healing of the area)
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stop up again, then put on a linen plug or cover, and let it stay overnight, and be taken out when the child wants to go into the chamber (i.e. go to bed). (This implies a temporary solution to prevent re-blocking of the baby's fundament)
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And if this blockage comes suddenly of a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to cover that suddenness: and let it be treated, just as we have said of the linen plug. (This implies a more serious condition requiring additional treatment)
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament (This suggests a specific medical condition being discussed)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are constricted, and grow larger when they come from outside the fundament towards it, or in the space between the two parts. (This implies a specific type of fistula, possibly related to the anal region)
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if it has one or more fistulas, and when that constricted one is old, it ulcerates, and the surrounding area becomes moist and whitish or subtle blue. (This describes a possible consequence of having an old fistula)
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas burst open; and are detected by those who see or experience emission or windiness when the patient makes an evacuation, and possibly by the jumping of a worm. (This implies that the fistula may rupture and release its contents, which can be observed by others)
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the junction of the vulva, and just to the edge of the knee. (This describes a specific type of fistula with multiple openings)
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows that the fistula has burst open at the fundament, and is not bursting. (This implies a way to determine whether the fistula has ruptured or not)
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. (This describes a procedure for diagnosing or treating a fistula)
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, then insert a thin linen tent or a horsehair until you feel the tent or the hair at your finger. (This describes how to navigate a tortuous fistula with a probe)
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission or windiness or worm coming out from the other end, as we have said. (This implies that the fistula may be blocked or not functioning properly)
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce through; you must hasten to cure it. (This suggests a course of action in response to a non-functional fistula)
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula bursts open just to the bladder or just to the urinary canal, it lets out urine, and cannot be closed by medications. (This implies a severe condition where the fistula is causing a continuous leak of urine)
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has pierced just to the junction of the vulva, then the tent or tube comes out through to the outside. (This suggests a specific anatomical relationship between the fistula and surrounding tissues)
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around it, then it means that there is a blue worm inside, and no medicine or binding with ointment can fix it. (This implies that the condition may be due to an internal obstruction or lesion)
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these burst-open fistulas there is no strong cure except the labor and vanity of foolish doctors who intervene. (This implies a skeptical or pessimistic view about the effectiveness of medical treatment for this condition)
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not burst-open and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced. (This suggests that the condition may be treatable with surgical intervention)
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on their back; and they lift their legs up to their vulvas, and have their vulvas inclined towards their belly. (This describes a specific position or preparation for a surgical procedure)
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert an iron tent, or linen one if there is tortuosity, as far as you know it comes out. (This describes the next step in preparing for a surgical procedure)
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then it is necessary that you insert your index finger. (This describes how to confirm the location of the fistula)
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if it feels then that the tent has pierced through; and you feel between your finger the sponge or the flesh, at that moment know that it is burst open. (This describes how to determine if the fistula has ruptured)
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if there is no remedy on which one cannot heal it. (This implies a sense of despair or resignation about the condition)
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says however that one can well heal some, but this happens rarely. (This suggests that there may be cases where treatment is possible, but they are exceptional)
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that we give to it, is that we heat a thin cauterizer according to the size of the fistula, as has been said before. (This describes one possible treatment method for the condition)
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and insert it hot into the fistula, as far as possible towards the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those charred fibers are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather. (This describes the process of inserting a heated cauterizer into the fistula)
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then heal it with moist linen tents until those burned fibers come out; and then treat it with ointment that hardens the char and closes it. (This describes a treatment plan for the condition)
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, then that's good. But if not, then it cannot be healed otherwise. (This implies a sense of finality or acceptance about the condition)
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent comes between, and does not pierce through to the very bottom which is the fundament, and there is a thick covering of char or sponge tissue between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at that place which touches the covering of the cure. (This describes a specific situation where the condition may be more complex)
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	so that you cover the beginning of the fistula and insert it directly in front of the tent, and then burn the cauterizer afterward, as far as it reaches to the head of the tent. (This describes a specific technique for treating the condition)
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and then the tent will be released and will close; and peel off those burned fibers that resemble a bird's feather, and none of them will remain. (This describes the final outcome of the treatment)
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the scar comes back, and forms a bond between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal sharpness. (This describes a possible complication of the treatment)
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For cauterizing with fire joins together two things: namely, the burning of those joined fibers and the drying out of blood and moisture. (This explains the principle behind using fire to cauterize)
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat it with moist linen tents or fresh cloths, until the wound starts to ooze and the burned fibers come out through the wound. (This describes a treatment plan for managing the wound after cauterization)
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with ointments that harden and dry out the skin, and are dried medicinal substances. (This describes a treatment plan for promoting healing and closure of the wound)
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it will be healed and will not come back again. (This suggests that with proper treatment, the condition can be effectively managed and prevented from recurring)
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the bottom of the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your finger or fundament, and investigate further. (This implies a need for closer examination or exploration of the area)
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between the two is the thread or sponge or fibers, or it is near to pierce, then there will be no more than a view of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: (This implies that the situation is precarious and requires careful consideration)
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you close it up to the bottom, or if you see fit, then insert tents and treat it as before. (This lists three possible treatment options)
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far in depth, lest you close the tent that holds the fundament, and make the evacuation come out against your will. (This implies a risk of causing more harm or complications if the treatment is not carefully managed)
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said. (This suggests that the treatment plan has already been discussed and should be followed)
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you will remove that covering and clean it afterward, since it has been closed up to the fundament, either by tent or by another instrument appointed. (This implies a possibility of successful treatment and recovery)
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then peel off that burned fiber which is in the wound, as far as you can. (This describes a final step in treating the wound)
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part opposite the fundament: if it is lighter for the patient.
