Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And whenever your fistula follows this manner: and when you plug the tent in the fistula, and it is on the opposite side of the fundament near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a tent with a hole at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one. I. cord twisted in two, and plug the tent into all the string in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the edge of the fundament inside, then pull out the string from that perforated one, so that you plug your two or fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the head of the string, and join the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and let it stay one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and bind it again whenever the threads are worn out that are between them, and they stick together.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in every way that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not necessary to pierce through the thickening that has formed if it is too deep inside, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula or spoon-like tool from which one makes the fistula is very sharp at one end and curved.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side, no (curved), for that's why you don't pierce what you shouldn't pierce, as you see here.
des emorroydes	the blood vessels
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Blood vessels are in two ways: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they bleed freely.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have less moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and they bleed freely or a little clear water or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the fundament is to have the patient strain himself in order to push out into a chamber, until the fundament lets out its contents and the threads appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if it's ready, and you hold it with tweezers, or between your fingernail, then pull it out at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the threads can't be held by their moisture, then take them up in one linen cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your arms, then cut them off, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cauterization.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you can cauterize them as is said in the treatise on cauterization, and then heal with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot come out, then have the patient take a purging enema with a bitter and sharp clyster to wash out what is in the fundament, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the patient is willing and if the strings are already out of the fundament, then this is a light treatment.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you grasp them with your fingernail or with tweezers and cut them off, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and so avoid the incision by iron (i.e., surgical removal).
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you need to sew the wound in this way: take one twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread upwards and make a hole through the other side of the needle, and turn both ends of the thread down along the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it's too wide; and strain the thread tightly, then tie the thread in a knot, pull out the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one to sew up any excess bleeding.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the fundament a damp linen cloth soaked in rosate oil or in cerote, and place it on the fundament, and tell the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him be until he is well again, and when they are fallen out, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the fundament.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dryness of the fundament in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine doesn't help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you need to scrape away the top layer of skin with a spatula or your fingernail, so that it doesn't leave any moisture.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat him as needed until he is fully recovered.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he can't recover, then start the scraping again more strongly than before, until he is completely healed and skinned over.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is fully healed.
dou fremit	from the fistula.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A furuncle is a small, false appearance around the body, and goes deep in. (Note: A furuncle is a type of skin abscess or boil)
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the furuncle finds its way to the muscle, and feels just like a dead fistula, and comes out all over the body, and more often in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a piece of raw goose quill or a strong chicken feather, and place it on the furuncle, so that the heat from the steam causes the furuncle to be surrounded entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand with the whole quill until you cut all around the furuncle, and put it deep inside, and remove the furuncle from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it's necessary, then make one from a piece of iron or steel in this form, and make it thin underneath and draw it upwards.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	don't make a hole, so that it can be held in the hand, and squeezed; and if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is said before or in the treatise on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	from the form of the clyster (enema).
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or gold, or molten iron or linen, and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to the form in which they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are made for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is above wide or the belly is joined in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an obstruction or the bowels are tied up, as you see, and the intestines are pierced inside; and there are two perforations on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and put the medicines of an animal bladder or parchment into it, and be pierced all around with small perforations.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have between each perforation one eighth of an inch's space, then put into these perforations one strong thread of green cord twisted ten or eleven times around, and sew up the belly as a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicines are inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then fumigate; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the syringe with oil or egg white or something similar, then put it in gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minster grasps the syringe in both hands together until it is completely void, then draw out the syringe, and raise up the sick person's legs to the pillow.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, let it drain as much as it can; and if he sleeps one whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have cleansed him with a syringe in the disease of obstruction of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament, or swollen, then have the syringe as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the delicate syringe above which the skin will be strained.
des plaies	of sores
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will say about the treatments of hands and of medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and of what kind they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by stumbling on a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or lance or club or spear, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will start with the head wounds, which are simple, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it's from stumbling on a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly of a hot apostema: if it heals quickly on its own from the head itself, even if there is pus coming out of the wound, and the healing occurs in contrast to the damaged part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and keep the patient full with wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not want to heal, thin out their meat, and do not let them drink wine, nor eat roasted meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound a poultice of moist cotton in rose oil or vinegar, to bring down the hot apostema.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot apostema, put on the wound a powder that I will speak of later, if the wound is fresh with all its blood and has not been moved by air.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has moved it, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot join together by themselves, then assemble them with stitches, just as I will say about belly wounds, in the chapter on stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to bone and open, and can only be held on by a little bit, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and order the patient to eat thick meats, such as roasted beef or bread cooked in a crust, also fowl and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find that the flesh is putrid and not connected to the bone, then scrape off all the pus, and let it bleed, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that is cut and cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loosened, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it's that you put this powder on them, which heals even when the air has moved in.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making this powder is: take one part of frankincense; two parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of galena, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, pressing it firmly, until it heals well and joins together with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then tie it tightly, and let it be without untying, if it does not swell; because one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this medicine only of galena, when there is no frankincense or dragon's blood, but the air has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the air has already moved the wound, even in its depth, do not put any of this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digesting ointments, or poultices made with barley flour, water, and honey, until it bleeds.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments, until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound and it's small, then stretch it with fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about skull fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the jugular vein or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the jugular vein, there is no other remedy than to leave it alone and not put anything compressing on it, because it hurts the vein and makes it retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the veins is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but apply the soothing medicine, such as galena washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and also washed cucumber in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones from the mine prepared in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have a lot of bleeding, then let them bleed out or lower down in that place.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and a lot of bleeding comes out, then tie it back together with thread, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the windpipe or trachea is cut, or the esophagus is torn, and the conduit is kept open by which the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so stitch the trachea above the canina of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then press gently on the wound, and let it be for some days, then treat it with ointments of decoctions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then tie it up.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then scrape them clean with forceps if you can, and as for what you cannot remove, let it be until the wound putsrefies.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and have it cut out and sewn up the exit.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed an abscess, then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds caused by a spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, look if there are signs of festering or swelling in the patient's groin area: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and is still fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder in at the first hour nor tie it up for fear that the blood will congeal and become stuck.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and cause gangrene to the heart, and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out all the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or longer.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if it does not come with a convulsion, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor training in the groin area.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	So then treat it with poultices and other remedies, until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and festering occurs, then know that there is an abscess; and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and it's superficial, or worse on the back, then treat it as you would for an open wound.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it's large, stitch it up; if it's small, use powder; and if it's pressed into the bone and has cut pieces, then tie the wound and scrape out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not scraped out, then let the wound putrefy, as it will help to loosen the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds in other limbs, judge them according to what we have said before.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the bursting of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The bursting of the belly is great, middle-sized, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound where sometimes the intestines or the veins of the intestines are pierced, through which the introduction of them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it's worse than a small wound that a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this, one has to reinsert the intestines with pins, if they are not put back in whole and whole.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they do not go back in with pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this, it is better to close the middle-sized wound, because one can sew the intestine back to its place with two threads.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the bursting of the belly occurs in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen when the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitching of other wounds in the body and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and always they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine protrudes.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if it needs to be put back together, it is done in one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one woolen cloth in sweet water only.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil it in sweet wine and cypress, and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and rinse the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine constricts and it is necessary to add only water to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or wine that has cooked onions in it.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this is helped the entrance to heal quickly.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch in the wound with the instrument used to lance boils.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is necessary before the cut.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without great necessity, lest there be an opening.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument for cutting through it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	which cuts into the fold and not on top, and look at this shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes out.
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then it should be put back in its proper place according to its natural form.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the part under the belly.
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so that you make the patient lie on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part under the belly.
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so put the head and the hips higher than the parts underneath.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the bursting of the belly is in one of the two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then place your attention on that which the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to heed what I say in large and middle-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds, put on what you are accustomed to.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands one ministerial piteous who holds all the bursting at his hand.
et assemble les levres;	and gather up the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or more, according to the size of the breadth of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave on the head of the wound two or three threads' length, and stick a needle where there is good strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two cheeks of the skin with the two needles of the siphach (a type of awl).
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the two ends of the siphach together in a knot.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then pull a double thread around the needle from both sides.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then join the two edges of the wound gently.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another thread's length, and stick another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the threads together just like you did with the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing it in this manner, using as many needles as you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is closed and restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are various in size, from fine to thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles pierce all the flesh and the too large ones cannot go in well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason it is necessary that they be various.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not help to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	because they will pierce and open up the wound in front of the stitches.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the tips of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when they sleep.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put poultices or cloths on the tips of the needles to keep them in place better.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is stitched together.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because only one needle or two are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you gather the two skin edges and the two siphach edges together with a needle that has a strong, medium thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these three edges together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews garments.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a thread's length between each stitch, of the size of a small thumb.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is known to housewives.
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that was on the belly of a horse.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been cut with a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's breadth in size.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it had protruded intestines of good two palms' length.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly itself.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I pulled back the intestine and it had been protruding for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed in just 15 days, and the patient cured, and was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where there was none to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put old cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outside part inwards, just until the point is inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced through the skin from right to left, then tie the thread of the siphach or costet where you have put the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside outwards, just until the point is on the outside again.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew like a furrier makes a pelt.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the siphach once on one side and take it back on the other, until the stitch is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which the Galicians call properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to gather the two parts together naturally in one place.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they fasten one end of the siphach to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	stick a needle or head of the mirach close by, and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the siphach.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part inwards, just until the point is inside again.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	the other shoulder of a sick person;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then drill one and the other from the outside part through to the inside with two more awls of iron that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the mother way of sewing and most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Galien said this phrase, and none can attest to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, or there be thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the sewing more grievous than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, in such a way as if fire had changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	so restore the intestine and the gut; then put on powder of calamine earth.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if fire has changed it, so put on any ointment that is present until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew the awl and the iron needle;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound just like the others until it is cleansed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, so put on old cotton as soon as she starts to heal,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it twice a day until it is cleansed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine except in some cases when the wounds are complicated.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound is making community with the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so it is convenient for you to anoint linen cloth lightly in hot thyme oil or in rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the joints and under the shoulder blades;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or burning in the bowels, and it happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	so cleanse him with black vinegar tea, and similarly if the burning comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce within it, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more light to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jun" cannot heal when it is hurt,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and that's because of the fragility of its vessels and because of the subtlety of all the body and the approach of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out from the wound, so put it back in just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it's old and has turned yellow or black, so it is convenient that you tie the part that is black, so that no bleeding comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the stitches.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put both ends of the string hanging down from under the wound until outside to relieve the extraction when the intestines come out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is rent, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	so it can be restored in some men.
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man hurt inside his belly with a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became gangrenous and turned into a fistula, and from there came diarrhea and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put him to heal according to what I knew, and did not stop subtlety until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the sickness would come back in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced men said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be stitched in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fine thread from great intestines, then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has gone through the mouth, so put it on top of both lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it closes her mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then the thread is tied at the end, and this stays so that he cannot untie it.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another thread afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This treatment preserves in the intestine and brings no harm to the sick person,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can suture the intestine with a fine thread tied from the intestine of an animal.
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread, which is quite clean and untainted,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread one fine linen thread twisted and turned.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle, and sew up the intestine, and then pull out the thread from the wound;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with thread is no less according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, or even in one of the principal intestines, there is no remedy nor healing, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be;
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it gangrenes, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it bursts and tears apart.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the hardness of its hard and white nodulation, where one does not feel pain;
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it bursts forth like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes bursts open wide and other times becomes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and other times large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and does not have flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not let new flesh grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because it has too much discharge;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or because the wound is putrid and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or because the treatment with medicine was not good;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is in the manner of a plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property of the place, where the digestion is slow and the healing is late, and that is by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting that I should tell you the treatment for a fistula, which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Abscesses occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are abscesses that come to the major veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the spleen, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or any of the joints of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and its natural place.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all abscesses that are in this manner are grievous for healing, and there is no other remedy than purging and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any abscess that does not come near the place I have said, and you have faith in its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you know it, take a lead or iron tube, if the abscess is straight, tie on to it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the abscess is twisted, search for a subtle sheet of linen;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the cloth will bend itself around the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the abscess has many perforations and you cannot search for it well with cloths,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	you should irrigate it through one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture spreads quickly from one pore to another, and purifies.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then tie it off tightly with the ligature at your skill, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and proceed carefully.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you about, then cut it according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and take out the decayed and corrupted flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then close it once it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the abscess is deep and in a right place, you should cut deeply, as far as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put wet cloths soaked in healing poultice and tie them just up to the head of the abscess.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine eats away the excess matter that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put salves in fresh good flesh until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the abscess, you should cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not hurt you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it out until all the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then close it with fresh good flesh as soon as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and you return to the same procedure as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the depth.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it becomes uncovered and you seek until you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there's no other remedy than to let nature take its course.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small piece of bone corrupted, and you can extract it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then extract them all, and leave none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut through the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something fresh on the wound to rot the pus.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the place around the bones is rotten.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then you will have them come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape away only the corruption until all the blackness is gone.
puis restoure la plaie;	then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of it corrupted and comes right up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then you should scrape it out and cut all the way to the corruption, and then close it until it is sewn.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about an abscess that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and have guidance in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from an internal cause within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	such that the matter came to the leg and was covered by a large abscess, and there was no external sign for it to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physicians, through their foolishness, made such a fuss that they forced the abscess to open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and it burst out and became a fistula, and there came out much pus that all the physicians were ashamed of and covered with shame.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians put ointments around for two years, but there was no skill in their manual art,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called and came to see his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which was flowing out through the fistula was very foul-smelling.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the boy's body became red and had a yellowish (citron-like) complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a tent into one of the fistulas, and then I searched all the other fistulas.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were connected to each other in all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hastened and cut into one of the fistulas until I uncovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be corrupted and perforated, with the corruption coming right up to the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what was showing from the corrupted bone, and I believed that there would be no other corruption than the one that I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to repair the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and found the bone as it was before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption continued in the bone, and I scraped it away, then removed it, and I set my mind to closing the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's length of bone and pulled it all the way out to its marrow.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I repaired it with medicines, and it was healed and sound quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to start again with the work except for the weakness of the sick person, who could not bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the bloodletting he often fainted, but he was entirely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was of good disposition, with no harm or contradiction at all, either as he lay there or when he came back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be scraped out in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and strain it to the head of the bone that is open.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another linen cloth of a larger size than the first one, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you can pull out the corrupted flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to scrape it, so that the scraping does not damage the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a wooden spatula over the bone to melt and cover the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape as far as you can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it;
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the flesh, then put a hot iron underneath.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one end to the other, and let the scraping be as long as the length of the corruption, that is, as much as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and scrape the bone on the other side where it contains.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, then there is no remedy except to cut them out.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or in the heel of the foot, it is very serious and strong.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you should inquire into that ulcer, how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but take care not to harm the surrounding flesh or the nerves.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knives and scrapers used to cut into bones are many, according to the size of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their coarseness and subtlety, their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare an instrument suited to each type of operation.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work itself will show you the tool that you will need, according to your knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways in which diseases manifest themselves.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the tool that you need, according to what is necessary for each case.
dou feu	from fire. (a return to a more poetic tone)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can become corrupted either from an internal cause or from an external one;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have given them medicine to treat the corruption, and it does not take effect.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cut off that member as far as the place where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the sick person may escape either by death or by a worse evil, namely the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then it becomes swollen after the blackness, and the corruption spreads from member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the whole body; so hasten to cut it out.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is from the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the vein, then cut it out, and do not give him a moment to come near as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it out at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that is death's door.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy except according to the quantity of his virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do the same thing when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut below the second joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises into the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or scraping the member is that you tie it on top and underneath,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one servant downwards with one cord, and another servant upwards with the other cord.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two cords to about the width of a spatula, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you cut or scrape it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the scraping does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and an abscess come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes from a vein when you operate, then cauterize the place quickly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or else put some restraining powder on it; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it until it is sound again.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to me in Somerset Place:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a burn appeared on him that seemed like coal from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the burn came first in his right foot, so much so that it covered all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the burn, he hastily had the foot bandaged and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the burn came back to his right hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that had a medicinal effect after the cleansing of the body, but the burns could not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of curing the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the man's virtue was weak and he completely lost hope and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastily bandaged his hand and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I've only told you this story because that's what we do in medicine when someone needs to be treated.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does a swelling come in the fatty part of the flesh, and stays so long that it makes a large gathering of boils;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and open up, and the boils jump out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is as thin as a delicate silk cloth;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not spread right to the bone or nerve, and diseases like this are called "boils".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so that you have to cut all around it, and itself when it's thin, just like a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have hope that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with fat, then let it be cured with a poultice.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look and see if the breast is large, and the boil that comes out of it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then let him be treated with an Egyptian medicinal poultice made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloe, oil, and lye, in equal parts, and put them together in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take what you need from it, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use the poultice to bind the breast, and close the opening (pertus).
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and the foul smell is gone.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never should it be treated with ash water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from a vine branch, and pour water over them.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then drain it, and use the liquid as a poultice, until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the sick person cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	should be used instead, with a little bit of lye beaten in.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you should poultice it with honey and sweet wine, for the honey has a property to cleanse and purify.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine helps to heal the flesh.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are hopeful that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then apply a poultice with those things which bring forth flesh in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take defrutum (or roselle syrup) and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you poultice it with various medicines and ointments, whose properties or how to treat ointments I have already mentioned.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the poultice cannot get into it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it a little with an iron tool, and apply an Egyptian ointment compress.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave just enough space so that the poultice can get in.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening from which pus comes out is at the top, then cut or lower it so that it is below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when pus is in depth, one should not let flesh form there.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut into the breast below as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus runs down to the lowest part.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the pus is deep, one should not let flesh form there.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut into the breast below as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so arrange it in such a way that the pus runs lightly downwards, and leave nothing of the pus.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and let it rest under a linen cloth that covers the whole breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at the strongest part of the opening of the breast, which is a little larger than the first one.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply soothing ointment on another cloth, according to the size of the opening.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the breast opening to ease the pus, and do not remove the large linen cloth outside until after a few days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that one on the breast opening, take away often to remove the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of the pus, if it is venom or a bit too much, or digestible, or not.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and be aware if the patient feels pain or no pain, and if there are any abscesses or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has taken this form and you see the nature that comes out on the breast opening,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healed already, and approach the patient.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then let him loose in the morning or on the third day, and when you untie the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast continues to discharge undigested pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom continues to flow after a long time, do not despair of recovery.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the health is approaching. For there are men who slowly form flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
