et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus continues to flow from the breast after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is ulcerated, then apply moist substances in consistency and dry virtues in potency.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as defrutum (or roselle syrup), because it contains a great part of vinegar, and this is the final medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defrutum (or roselle syrup), and mix it with rose oil, and add the sap of old equalized wine in consistency.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same thing with honey that is cooked and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defrutum (or roselle syrup) is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and beat them into a powder, and sprinkle it on the honey while it is on the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then tie up the cloth, and put it on the breast, and do not remove it for a long time, administer or not an astrolabe.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of heaven, which is also like flour of violets and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them in simples or compounds: crush them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is old-fashioned and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has gone deep, and has made impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so apply a treatment for the abscess of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the suppurating boil.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pus is a kind of boil that comes out under the finger of the fist.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or under the toe, or perhaps it occurs in other fingers.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and becomes old, then a hot boil comes out of it.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and discharge pus as long as the root of the boil is running, and perhaps they drain all of it.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and then comes corruption just to the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the abscess of the boil is large and has a dark, bloody color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section on boils, and the treatment does not bring any benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must cut out all the remaining superfluity from the boil with a sharp instrument.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the boil is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the boil approaches the flesh and begins to fester and break open,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should put an ointment on the boil that touches the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and bind it tightly at the top, and cut out the subtle and delicate skin around it.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining skin medicines that burn and corrode in order to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has reached the bone, then cut it out, and remove any further corruption, for as long as the corrupting bone is present, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the sinew corroding, then cut out the affected part of the tendon as was said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and causes great pain, then you should first try to heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the boil on the pustule deeply across, cutting diagonally above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not reach as far as the skin underneath the boil, for the sick person would feel too great a pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then apply something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the abscess in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The tendons that swell in some men's hands, perhaps because they are all flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps it has this kind of swelling where there is bone and no boil.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and sometimes they occur in the root of the joint or in certain tendons of the hands.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that occur in any tendon of the hand cannot be moved,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that occur at the joint of the hand, perhaps can be moved.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut on one who is all flesh is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who occurs in the root of the joint is hard to cure, and you must hold on to cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	When one occurs at the last tendon, it is necessary that you cut around the surrounding flesh up to the bone first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate thread for this kind of thing, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The burn or scald that comes to the hands together comes from birth, or a wound, or a burn of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out the scalded area, so that the tendon can repair itself according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or damp cloths in rose oil, so that they do not adhere together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is healed, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If scalding comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that scalded area as it is necessary.
Des vils	The boils on the palms.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Blistered boils are large, swollen and full of melancholy pus that occur in multiple parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer them sometimes an evacuation of gall and then cleanse with the white of egg.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is to cut them out, and then drain the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the blister, and let it all drain.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut is made in this way: first, heat the leg with a very hot iron, so that the thick skin is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strip the patient's leg from the top of the knee down to the part under the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut out the blister in one place, or in two places, or in three places with a wide knife.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then let it bleed and drain out the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient's virtue can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up and command the patient to eat meat that causes dark black gall to form.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the blisters are full and cause harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The removal of hair from the leg is in this way: shave the patient's leg if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it [the skin] in a bath and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the blisters swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then cut in that place where the blister is, at the top of the kneecap or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with a hot iron, and scrape out the blister from each side, until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put on the strip over it, until it is raised from the skin, and then tie it with a light thread.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place above the three fingers, and then scrape out the skin over the blister until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift up the strip, as you did, and tie it with another thread, just as you tied the first one.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision or several if needed, then lift up the strip, and cut it at the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then drain and lift up to the second incision, then pull it out from incision to incision, until it comes out completely, and then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you can't drain and lift it, then insert a needle with strong thread into each filament, doubling it up.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and drain it, and insert the thread into each filament, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't cut, because if it does cut, then you can't drain or lift it out, and it will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drained it completely, then put a damp wool pad soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the blister is contracted and twisted together, and not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it across, but do not cut all the way through, and drain it just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife that is used to cut the blister is curved, and does not cut all the way through, so that it cuts into the blister.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a thick curve, because if it were thin, it would cut into the blister itself, but rather thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil or common boil.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This kind of boil is formed in hot parts of the legs, where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground where there is little moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it occurs in other parts of the body besides the legs, and this comes from filth that rises up from the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	such as comes from worms and serpents inside the body, which are formed between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this boil are that it comes to the leg as a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the boil begins to come out like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the abscess is open, it is necessary that you wrap a cloth of linen around from one and a half to two fingers, and tie it up.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it gets wet, wrap it around the cloth again and tie it up.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining part around, but do not cut into its root until it has come out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and filth to form in that place, and a bad disease will result.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of this reason, it is necessary that she be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this boil is when it is being treated from five to ten finger-widths long.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man came to me, whose it came out ten finger-widths long, and when you cut it, he put in a thread or a string, and pierced it down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out, and the matter inside is emptied out, and medicine to prevent filth or purulence is administered to the place every day, then it is treated just like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes to this vein, many remedies are needed; and indeed when it opens in the joint of the foot, or at the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it bursts out with pus, and from which a foul odor arises; therefore cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox" because it has happened many times to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and the patient feels it well as it moves from member to member, until it tears the skin where it goes and bursts out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is in danger of being corrupted by some humors, such as come from worms and snakes and lice and roundworms or the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and we doubt its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it may penetrate and destroy the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one can hardly escape when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong thread tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then scrape on top and pull out, and if the worm is deeply in the flesh, and you don't find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so cauterize with fire on top, until it burns.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then bind a thread tightly under it in shape of a circle, then scrape on top and pull out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient with purifying remedies for body diseases from corrupting humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and let them abstain from meats that cause corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those things that I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the upper arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and little by little, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, just like bright silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was twisting around the body, just as I had seen it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen that disease behave in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen well-known physicians allow the pain to move from place to place;
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it happen as I did see in that woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a weak body and the veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore that windiness appeared constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear in those who are well-nourished and have moist bodies and well-covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if they tell you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then lay on top of it a thread tightly above and below, and then scrape on top until the windiness has been expelled from that place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize that place; and if you do not see improvement in them,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then use remedies to expel the windiness, such as foul-smelling pills and viper's pills and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small, and hairy, and tied on;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with two edges, and those with claws, and of those that have fragments or splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that lodges in any member does so in two ways: either it lodges in the main member, or it is lodged under the ligament;
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, liver, spleen, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it lodges in any of these places, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so be warned to beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows afterwards in various forms.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if you do not see that bad sign, and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces it and lodges in the skull, and you see a piece of flesh flying forward that is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is a sudden and great darkness, and a deep sleep, and vertigo, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perchance it happens without pain in the nostrils or ears; and perchance it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound there comes out a moist white discharge, like pus, and also as black as charcoal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see this sign, then be on guard for the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not already gone.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the spleen when it is pierced by the arrow are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the spleen becomes swollen like pus, and flows with black blood, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you should be certain without doubt that death will ensue.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never lodges in the navel are: there is a foaming discharge coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and sighs loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow lodges in the covering of the liver, it is located near the small ribs; and there is a great pain and a great agony, and the sick person sighs; and the muscles of all the members of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow lodges in the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the abdomen and there is no passing of feces through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and urine comes out and flows away, and the sick person feels a great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, arms, neck, shoulders, and armpits, and the spine of the back, and the ribs, and the hips, and the thighs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow pierced the eye in the root of the nerve:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and was cured without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out a arrow that had pierced the fatty part under the paper of the eye socket,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck and I could only feel the tip towards the front.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as thick as a Turkish bow string, with all its iron point without ears; the youth was healed, and no bad consequences came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loosened the feathers, and made it so fine that I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from a man, who had been pierced in the stomach, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after 30 days, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and tied a knot, and pulled it out, and there was no bad consequence.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow has pierced the back, and the wound is stitched up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did he find any trouble in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, whose arrow pierced his face, and the wound was stitched up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and thus he remained without suffering great pain; and many others similar to him.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the king's sons, who had it pierced in the eye:
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and he was leaning to the right side, and the arrow was completely stuck.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat him after it had been pierced three days. And I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for the arrow with great subtlety and did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow,
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put a plaster on him that is attractant and digestive, so that the place would not become inflamed.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the spot from the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put a plaster on it for several days and the wound was resolved again, and the patient remained so for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his eye; and he told it to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicament that is caustic and corrosive for several days, until it was completely open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to pull it out, and felt the head of the arrow which had come out at the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that caustic medicament, until the tip of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the tip passed well around three months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I closed up the wound that I had put forceps on, and stitched it from one side to the other, but it couldn't be made to come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I didn't stop trying and tying with various instruments, until I managed to get hold of it one day with good forceps.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was stitched up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows:
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may put your cure on what I have not said, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can remedy well enough with a small thing, and with what is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works, and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the arrows do not come out from the members where they are stuck, except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another place.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that one which comes out through the other side is an arrow entering a fleshy part and coming out once again at this time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, let it be left until the flesh is putrid around it, and the issue is clear.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it be left for some days, and turned every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if not, pierce around with a very sharp needle, until the surrounding area is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have told you will appear to the patient: do not pull it out at all, but let it stay until it is calm after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes up to the forehead, it is mortal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck no further than in the bone alone, and does not come up to the forehead,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient will remain for some days without any bad consequences, if it is tied off with a string for pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, I administer theriac around it, as I have told you before; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the flesh of the body so that it cannot be seen, then seek out a good surgeon.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with some suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in its way, then cut it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has feathers to which it is attached,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut away the flesh that is stuck on both sides of the wound as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the feathers of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out more carefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the surrounding area is putrid, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be clearer.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding from the wound makes you contrite, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the incision to the nerve and vein, and set a remedy so that you can pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently, and put the patient in the shape that he was in when the arrow pierced him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that he can be, and if you cannot do this, then put him in a position according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes out from the other side, or it makes some sign of itself, or the skin is swollen in the place where one can see or feel it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut above it, until the forceps can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it alone for a while, and then start the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is in, then insert into it as much of the shaft as possible.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft splinters and you need to apply some kind of glue, then administer a caustic instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument, and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, then insert into it an instrument with a sharp tip going in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, it is advisable that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it seems best.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces in the chest or belly or bladder or side and is close to something important, and you can cut on top, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the caustic instrument is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to insert it into the tip of the arrow, as shown here is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for inserting and checking if it's like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	arteries of the common body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one bleeds are 31, and it has 16 branches at its head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: the two pouches that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two apparent temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead, and the vein that is at the head of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two grooves that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on top of the lips, and they are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins from which one bleeds, in each arm, are five:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the first is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the second is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic vein and the basilic vein.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it "vein of the heart", and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it a "wound of the belly", and it is on the navel.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that is the wound from which one can see the intestines, which appears obviously above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvadelle is the vein that is between the thumb and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one of them is under the bend of the left knee's socket.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein that is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The swelling of the veins that are behind the ears helps the ancient catarrhs and hemicrania.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the remedy, as I said, is that you raise the head of the sick person.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place or veins with a rough cloth; then squeeze the sick person's neck with a vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two small hanging pieces from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and then apply them to your throat, and where you feel the pulse under your throat, it should beat strongly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand with the whole vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and separate the skin and the vein very carefully on both sides of the crossing, and let out as much blood as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it tightly, until it is sound;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth to migrate old age;
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and to be used for dropsy and ophthalmia accustomed, and to put an end to sharp tears themselves.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the surgeon if it is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient strains his neck so much that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse under your thumb, and then signs it off.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift up the key above the vein upwards to your index finger, and put the lancet under,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you have done in the other two veins, and make a small incision according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on a compress.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly, and let it be until it is sound; and we have already spoken of its incision and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the vein of the forehead is worth just as much as the bloodletting from the cerebral vein in ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for jaundice.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting it, so much so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the point on the vein, and press up with your hand, or something else, and let the blood come out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then untie the patient's neck and bind the vein so that it is sound, and once the work is done, apply a broad bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable for the bandages to be too tight; and for the bloodletting to be done in such a way that it crosses over, because the bone is close by, and it may break through the bandage if it becomes too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the two temples is very helpful for them, and for jaundice, and for yellow fever, and for eye problems such as oriel in the eye, and for diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck by twisting it from any ligature, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed, and the bleeding of the forehead should be about the length of the width of the bandage plus a little bit on each side, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandages are thin, it may break through; then make a small incision in the blood, as much as you need, and then apply compresses on top of cotton, and tie them tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bloodletting from the vein of the nape is worth for ague, and for epilepsy, and for diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and jaundice that come to the face, and especially when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck, then stretches out his nape with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the thin and long bandage, and place it in the space between the two nostrils, on the upper lip.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein will not appear well there, and the blood will now begin to come out.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't let it go too far into the forehead, and make a small incision in the blood according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the shape of the bandage:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bloodletting from the two temples is helpful for the constriction of the uterus, and the beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for epilepsy, and for scrofula, and for ulcers, and for herpes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck under one and then the other, just as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and it should be the master (the physician) standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on a stool.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the long vein somewhat widely, then take out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and strain the blood moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and let him leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bloodletting of the temples
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting from the veins of the upper lips is helpful for ulcers in the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and fissures of the lips, and of the nape and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bloodletting is to have the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right side of the upper lip, and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by the fact that they are black, and because around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then take both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then take the largest one from each side, and do exactly the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bloodletting under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bloodletting from the veins that are under the tongue is helpful after bloodletting from the cephalic vein, and it's for constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed both of them, but do not go too far in depth, because under those are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck that one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a very large bandage that pierces through to the middle of the neck, or with an olive-sized thin needle, as you call it "anasil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and their width and thickness depend on the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the very large bandage is well-known, and it's wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to be used to open up the thick veins that contain large and turbid blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of the olive-shaped bandage:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more fine-pointed, and it's used to bleed the thin veins, where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bloodletting of the Basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is helpful for diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bloodletting to be done carefully, so that he does not touch the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he touches the artery and a hemorrhage of blood comes out, then it is necessary to tie him up, as I said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be pierced with the bandage, but rather cut like a scalpel (anasil).
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the Basilic vein does not appear obviously, it is necessary to strain and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want to take some of its blood, or you bleed in place of it the vein in the arm: it appears obviously.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the bandage like a scalpel (anasil), as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the bloodletting, it is necessary then that you strain the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you can feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the bandage like a scalpel (anasil).
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the spot swollen, because it is the artery: avoid that place then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it's blood from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your finger on top lengthwise, then take out your finger if the bleeding stops, which happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then tie up the arm, and leave it like that, and don't move the patient until he is healed. And be on guard, and don't move him as long as he is recovering.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it's urgent, and there are no remedies present, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will pull back; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig tree bark, and cut it in half, and take one of the halves and tie it tightly up to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding has stopped, that's good; if not, then apply the powders that stop blood, as we have said.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the clotting is not delayed in more than a few days for the small wound and the strength of the ligature of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bloodletting from the vein in the middle is helpful for drawing out blood from the head above and the chest below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the Basilic and Cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the bloodletting to be done carefully so as not to touch the nerve that is underneath, and if he pierces too deeply, he will find the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the healing process is delayed, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve appears many times, and if it doesn't appear in some people because of its subtlety, it is necessary that you bleed with the instrument like a scalpel (anasil); and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, cut them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting from the Cephalic vein is helpful for drawing out blood from the head, and it helps itself.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it's necessary to bleed with an olive-shaped bandage or a very large bandage, because it's the safest of all veins, since there are no nerves or arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to find the lightest spot, and not to tire anything if we fail the first time, and we will try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, the spots may swell in some people when we fail to bleed them at first, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is not accomplished except by preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent illnesses from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the healing is done in one of the three ways that are or cut: that is to say, cerebral, visceral, and basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must heal in the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three double days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing which is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but whenever there is need of day or night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not agree to heal children until fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying more than four weeks until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one be healed who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light purge.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the superfluities which are harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal who is too salted with meats, nor who is drunk, as long as they are so, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one must be careful not to heal after a bout of severe colic, vomiting, and bowel distress, and multiple times giving birth to a woman, and hard labor, wakefulness and sleeplessness, and all the virtues, or by something from the arm or from the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purge the humors subtly, if the bile is thick, by means of meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath or plunge in water, unless something prevents it, in order to purify the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and then heal from the vice of the stomach around the third time, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be happy and joyful, and the healer should be higher than the one being healed, and strike the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament above in a gentle manner, because when it is too tight or loose, the bile cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with the hands, until the veins swell and become sensitive.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the healer's flame with a small amount of old oil, and then place the tip of his left hand on top of the sick person's vein below the affected area.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst and bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	Because there are veins that burst like strings when being healed, and some of this type that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when the flame is put on, it retreats and cannot open up the vein, and thus one becomes of this kind.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts open the vein, then the wound is too tight, therefore it is necessary that the healer be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts open at first time, that's good; if not, then he starts again a little below or above the same spot, as long as the skin is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the skin is swollen and the sick person is afraid, then he leaves it for one or two days, and does not bind up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come festering boils; do not take a bath, then try to heal it again if he likes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small or the bile flows subtly and you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, then take the whole flame directly into this same wound.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and let it work a little bit quickly, so that the skin becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the skin become swollen, do not try to heal it again, and put a little bit of linseed oil on it, because it lightens the body of the blood and is good for this place where the oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil in every healing of veins that you perform, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is also made from onions and vinegar, when you put it on the skin; it purifies the bile and separates it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large festering boil that has formed many times, especially when it is not healed strongly enough or the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hurry and put on the spot a moist sponge in warm water and vinegar for a short while, and squeeze it out for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if it remains at the spot for some days without any blackness or greenish color, then it does no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see anything, put on something of aloe or myrrh that has been made into juice with camphor, wormwood, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been an abscess and an appearance at the healing of the basilica: then put your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put on anything of what we have said, for perhaps it will cut the artery's blood; but make a dry plaster to harden the spot, and then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its amount of blood and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins; and if it's too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is bloated and swollen, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the incision be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to one who is weak, do the opposite, and let them be healed little by little, and it should be healed cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from the bleeding of blood and the cutting of nerve, and it's worth more than the long cut or the wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body is failing from the bleeding, it's necessary to give a damp cloth in juice of crushed apples; if they are heated, let them take away the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold complexion, let them take the damp cloth before the bleeding in syrup of must or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they are fainting from the bleeding, after the flow of much blood, it's necessary that they smell a broth of meat and sweet-smelling syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use all the other things we have said in the chapter on fainting, for evacuation of bile.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to relieve his arm, and heal it again another time, when it is weakened by great bleeding, he should bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuing.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong pulse, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another place, he should be bled on the second day or the third.
