Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood inside the body that is already heated up, and makes fever; so it should be let out in great quantity, and the puncture should be widened until it reaches the peritoneum.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you observe all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come instead of peritoneum.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the bleeders is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it's not necessary when you see that the arm is unfastened and blood is coming out the second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press strongly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless it's curved, let him stretch his arm quickly, for that would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave him alone until he bleeds the second time; or you can prick at the tip of the flame, so that the blood which is coagulated comes out easily again.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .i. pot of linen soaked in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it again, until the inflammation has been alleviated.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are bled instead of the main vein because they are composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient dips his hand into hot water, until the fistula is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be tied loosely, so that the vein appears well, then let him bleed now across, not too wide or too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the puncture should be large and let him bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put his hand in hot water again, and let the blood drain into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's in summer, then don't put his hand back into hot water, for one puts the arm more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, since there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the basilic vein on the right hand is worth it for all diseases of the liver, and this is how to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	stretch out the hand and dip it in hot water, until the vein swells and can be seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cut across and take the whole vein, then nothing is harmed.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too deep, because the nerves are all bare underneath the flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is coagulated in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is needed, then put oil and thread on the vein to close it quickly, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding on the left hand is worth it for the disease of melancholy, and do everything in the same way as I told you to do with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The bleeding on the saphenous vein is worth it for all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the womb, and retention of urine, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient dips his foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it swells.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and it runs from there up to the foot in many reins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	bleed then in the largest rein or the one at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed above the foot, then be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and make sure to cut across in bleeding, so that the flesh is not split.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot back in the water and let it drain completely from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding fails the first time, then start again the second time above a little bit, because the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	don't doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and do the same thing with the saphenous vein of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee's back, and its bleeding is worth it for the pain in the groin, when it's bloody hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient gets into a warm bath and stretches above the knee 4 fingers in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein won't appear; and if it does appear, then bleed in all ways that you can, and cutting across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it's worth just as much if you cut it, because the place is salty, and it's very accustomed to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you can't find it, then bleed any vein that appears above the foot or behind the knee, and towards the little finger, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do as much bleeding as you see fit, then untie the tie, and put on some cotton and tighten it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	It seems like we're moving on to a new topic! The next section appears to be about bleeding using a venetian treacle or a vacuum cup (ventouse). Would you like me to continue translating this part?
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venetian treacles are made of horn, or metal, or glass; and venesection is done in two ways: either by cutting to attract blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this venesection that is not with cutting is done in two ways: either it's on the fire (i.e. scalding hot), or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and venesection that is done by cutting and the extraction of blood is done in 14 places on the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	in one of them it's at the top of the head, and the others are in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more on each side of the neck; and the one under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ones at the elbows, and those above the hips.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ones in the two arms, and the ones in the two legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the ones at the two ankles; and venesection does not bleed much blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it is not weakened anyone much, as one would do with bleeding of vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable that it be administered, neither with fire nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for habituation, let us administer each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and at midday and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find repletion and darkness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and shadows over themselves.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are bleeding internally.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who see visions, and perceive through blood and wounds and bites and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it's in the middle of the month, we will order them to bleed after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the muzz (a type of vein) helps with the grievousness of the head that comes from themselves, and it is not advisable to do it after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this venesection is in place of bleeding of the cerebral vein.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it's not advisable that someone with a cold complexion uses it, or who has a catarrh, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it's not advisable that the elderly use it, nor those who have or had cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who bleed themselves often, become forgetful, and for this reason it's advisable to put the venetian treacle a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The venesection in the neck is in place of bleeding of the head and the base of the brain, and for this reason it's worth it for the tightening of the stomach.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to bursting of the channel of the womb, and at childbirth, and in cases of repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it's advisable to put a little pressure on it, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart trouble.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The venesections on the two sides of the neck are worth it for headaches, eye pain (obtalmie), and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it's in place of bleeding the base of the brain; and you should command the bleeder to express his hand in such a way that he does not cut the artery, and does not bleed too much blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venesections under the chin are worth it for diseases of the mouth, and for decay of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and they take the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The venesections at the elbows are worth it for diseases that come from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The venesections on the arms are worth as much as bleeding of three veins in the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the bleeder not to cut too deep in front, because the place is bare of flesh and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venetian treacle which is on the hip is worth it for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases beneath, and it's necessary that the treacle be large and made of metal, so that it can bleed well; and if it were thin, it might break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesections of the legs bleed openly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth it for old pains in the veins, and in the kidneys, and in the bladder, and they cleanse the pustules; and they take the place of bleeding from the two saphenous veins, and from the two ankles, and however, they weaken the body after long use, and cause pallor in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the venetian treacle is that you first put it empty and then fill it with blood, place it quickly, move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the vein turn red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then cut, and reapply the venesections, and pay attention to the condition of the body, because there are those who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, one must cut only once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to cut twice: the first time to thin out the large vein of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to cut a third time; and when we want to draw out some blood little by little, we can suffice with only one cut.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we should start again often; and if the blood is thick, let's cut deep, and the ends are such that the heart can be perceived suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the areas of the venesections with oil that is apt and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's with ointment of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's with yew, with oil of chicory, or lily, or chamomile, or similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person to whom we are bleeding has tender flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on them.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or morel water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very damp, should get up with the aid of myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should get up with old wine, or vinegar of juniper, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable to bleed with a venetian treacle before bathing or in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours; and do not sleep after bleeding.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it's necessary that he wash himself when he needs to be bled and when he is being bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who bleed themselves are choleric, and the blood is too sharp and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it's necessary that he takes cool things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces to aid digestion, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young wine, and meat of rooster, and moistened meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and a medium-aged wine that is between old and new, and little wine, and young wine, and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day on which he will be bled, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people some time before bleeding or after, to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned out, but it's not advisable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The venesections that are not put to cut are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the lower back, because these members do not tolerate being cut on them.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it only to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the shoulders when a new person is bleeding, to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just like how we put venesections on the belly and on the navel to reduce the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain, when there is a clot or abscess, it removes by its attractive virtue, perhaps the clot, or draws out the pus from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so does it when put on the liver and spleen when there is retained venesection.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these venesections are administered empty to suck out only, and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the tear sac, and in this manner one fills the venetian treacle with hot water alone, or with water that has boiled herbs suitable for that purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the venetian treacle administered with fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	and has 2 thumbs of width and half a palm of depth, and on the side near the middle it has one small perforation, just like for putting in a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is made of metal, soft at first so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle has a rod of iron or steel crossing over, to hold a candle in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are made large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the venesections for children are different from those for old people, and for thin ones than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus put this venetian treacle on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	light the candle with wax or a liniment, and put it in the venetian treacle across the rod that is inside the venetian treacle.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the venetian treacle, and it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and the two ends should be above the perforation that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, the vapors can escape, and then take out the venetian treacle.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the liniment just like before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the venetian treacle used for disease of the tear sac, there is no rod nor perforation, and it is not administered with fire unless it is filled with water, and it is put on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	venesections are not administered with fire except in members where one cannot put venetian treacles because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places bare of flesh, such as toes or heels, and others like them.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of use is that when you find venesections that are in sweet and pure water without any sedimentation, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and soak them in sweet water for a long time until they are well known and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be bled with vein and venetian treacle, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the venesections.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and have become hard, if it is a place where one can put a venetian treacle, then put it there, because this helps a lot afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place with a gentle aid, and then with water, very well, and then press it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place bleeds too much from the body of the venesections, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the blood is congealed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is plentiful, put on vitriol that has been bruised or gallstones and similar things, until it is congealed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	You place a hot poultice of peeled peas on the middle of the joint, and let it stay until it cools down to the joint; it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the poultices do not want to take hold, rub the joint with fresh blood, or you stick a needle in it until the poultice comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and at once as they feel the blood, they will heat up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are sweating, sprinkle on a little aloes and burnt linen or ashes, and they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is very often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for breakage and swelling.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish people fall from this chapter, which they never saw in any ancient book, nor did they read about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of that reason is the science strange in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have written about it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described it to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we now say the prologue of this book, which contains the summaries of words and chapters where the wise person puts their understanding, and remains on virtue, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten and treat the sick person from both sides, and if anything is lacking in your power, such as weakness of body, infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is very cold or too hot, and you have a fever that is not good, such as a cold temperament, and a body of bird meat and goat flesh, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain of a warm aposteme or bursting of matter in the member; then return the sick person to their primary governance as they used to use.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the sick person with meats that make a thick and viscous flesh, such as bread cooked in water, and rice, and cheeses, and pieces of beef, and veal belly, and onions, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the flesh will knit together more quickly and the break will heal sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old people and those who are decrepit cannot well knit together or heal according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor also those who are too soft, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, scrape off the broken bone with a rough iron file that has been heated and join the member together, so that it strengthens itself as it was before; and do not remove too much of his flesh, and because of this it is necessary to nourish him with thick meats, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that broken bones are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the back, or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that a bone can be broken.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go across the joint, and others that are oblique, such as the break of a quill's nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is also a break with a cut, and a break with a small slit in it all at once.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own method and proper instrument in the restoration, according to how the break heals itself.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that a bone is broken by what the place looks twisted and clearly open from outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if there is no twisting or snapping sound, and the sick person does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can very well have a twist, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move the hand, but rather apply medicine that comes later, and then immobilize it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go across and separate the two parts, it is necessary to now put them together equally, so that warm apostemes come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if warm apostemes come, then you should leave them alone for a day or two, until the apostemes are calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then put it back together equally to the way it was lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of the joint is easier than the restorations of that which has pieces; then immobilize it, as is necessary later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and they can be held together with two parts of thread, if it's hands or feet, or if you have a small member at hand, or if it's two threads, or if it's one thread and your own hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back together according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are aligned, use all possible means to scrape away the added bits from their places with a thread, and be sure that through your work, no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and firmly fasten together the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well done: then straighten it beautifully, and do not immobilize it too much, nor press as those who bring about warm apostemes and contractions in the member do, as we have warned many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, then punish the patient so that they do not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take good care that the member is so secure that the patient feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it does not feel any pain, then it is not in place, and you need to put it in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed correctly, so that there is no twisting when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in size and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: it is necessary to wrap them gently in soft and fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong linen cloth, for the broad cloths enclose all the large member and bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no crease.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light strips of linen cloth around it, three or four times depending on the member, and bind your hand to a small piece at the end of the cloth, then go above the break and bind less tightly than the break itself, so that the break will be slightly apart from each other.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the cloth a little bit and a little bit more, until you take up most of the healthy flesh, then take another strip of linen and turn it around again on top of the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said in the first layer above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put linen or cloth pads in between the bandages, as long as it is all even, then tie everything together with one strip of cloth, and then put your properly made pads on top, if there are no swellings or effusions.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or effusion, then put on something soothing and warm that will calm the swelling and remove it, and leave it like that for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind the pads with a strip of cloth that is about half an inch thick and well-made, or made from the wood used to make knives, or palm splints, and be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the pad placed on the break is a little bit bigger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is needed for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind the pads on top in the same way as you did at the first layer, then tie a thread on top gently, just like in the first layer above the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it should be tighter on top, less and less; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, it's like the works of fools who make their stitches with linen cords twisted into knots, and that's a great error, because the stitch cannot be even if it's too fine, and it should not have less than two or three spaces between each pad.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the edges of the pads after they have been applied in their place, then put linen or torn cloth under them so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the sinew is broken, I will tell you the treatment later. (This seems to be a transition to a new topic or section in the text)
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind with pads all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put on pads until after five days or seven days, or more according to your judgment in case of warm swelling occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the ancient method of applying pastes to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is kept near the walls of a mill, mix it with abundant egg yolk, and make this concoction neither too clear nor too thick. Use it, and this is the common method for restoring breaks in many situations, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: take 3 parts of absinthe, ladanium, myrrh, and aloe wood, ana .x. (parts), and add 5 parts of mirre, ana .v., and 8 parts of aloes, ana .viiij., make it into powder, and mix with abundant egg yolk; if the complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for twists: take mugwort and vervain, ana .x. parts; mirre and aloes, ana .viiij. parts; myrrh resin, ana vi parts; Armenian bolic, ana .x. parts, and grind them well, and mix with vinegar or abundant egg yolk, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that are disjointed from their places, and calms the pain accompanying it, and is used to treat fractures: take new linen, moisten it with vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area. This plaster does not restore, but it is good for calming hot swellings and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and ground ivy (also known as "pavol terrestr" in old French), grind them together and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone breaks and to reduce the remaining swelling. Take roots of vervain, camomile, violet flowers, and flour of each one part; grind them together and mix with wine. If the member is overheated, mix it with moist coriander water or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plaster that is stronger than the previous one, when hard swelling comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of vervain, flax seeds, balaustinum, mellilotus, and violets, all in equal parts; grind them together and mix with salt water or sweet water or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member to restore it except for a wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two temperatures, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member things that are a little bit warm and dry, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar substances, which we have already mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort, threads from the tail of a castrated man or goose feathers, and vervain, all in equal parts, grind them together and make a plaster to bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove the plaster a little while later and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone returned to its place, do not remove it for a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain, itching, or swelling comes to the place, or a redness appears, be quick and remove the plaster, and take off the plaster now; and take some light cloth, and wet seaweed sponge, and dip it in water, and lift up the affected area until the itching ceases and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen that has been moistened in water or rosed oil, and bind it with a cloth strip, as long as you are certain of hot swelling.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member be calmed down and the pain be removed, then repeat the delicate binding and a little bit of plaster, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and gently continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have been completely removed, and you need plaster and cloth bandages again, then repeat it, just as you did the first time in the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the member, then do not remove it until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and at no time let it remain for more than 20 days, as one sees fit, until the break is healed and approaches the joint again.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then the restraint will be more than before, and the flesh will thicken, as I said before; and if you see that the place is drying out more than necessary, know that putrefaction cannot come from it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	take a mixture of hot water and vinegar to wash the place, every time you remove it, and do this for each third day, and slightly loosen the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work, the putrefaction is cut from the member, and it heals quickly, unlike the evil works of fools who restored the member wrongly: this is bad, and I see only laziness and a lack of proper working.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It looks like we've reached the end of the text. The author seems to be concluding by highlighting the different ways in which breaks (or fractures) can occur.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breakings, and various shapes, and their causes are appointed.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breakings that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the elbow breaks all the bone right down to the spongy part which is under the bone, as if it were an axe or wedge; and for this reason such breaking is called "hache" or "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above so as to pierce it, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound of these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an enclosed percussion, or fracture, or breaking of the elbow by stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is reunited with the bone as subtle as a thread, and this fracture is small, and for this reason it is called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by hitting with a stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes the piece of bone go inward, and it forms a hole like those that blacksmiths make when they hammer on the furnaces, then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have or have had soft bones, such as the heads of children.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and this happens to all these manners of breaking where small pieces are pulled out, such as those; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we are familiar with all manners of breaks by their appearance on them, and the investigation that has been done, and through the corrupted flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently with a cloth, if the break shows black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, take note of the patient's adverse conditions, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, bruising, fever ague, or the like to appear, and all this with a sure and certain sign, then he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no alarming accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone is corrupted, and come the accidents which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes just up to the tissue that covers the brain, then you should split the broken part thus: and it is that you take hold of the head of the wounded person, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and above the appearance of the wound as soft as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the discharge of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess forms, then the aid from those who it is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloth moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest as long as the abscess is calmed and you are assured of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and it is done in two ways of operation: one way is that you cut at the narrowest part before, and this shape is:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another cutting, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have various types of stitches, some thick and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron wire; and work lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, then it's necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer stitches with awls, but not too deep that they penetrate through the thin part of the bone on top; and should have above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point doesn't pass through the bone; and you'll need to have several, so that each one goes back into its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for all bones; and this is the shape of the three kinds of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl above the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone has been pierced; then put the awl elsewhere a little further along, and so do everything around, then clip with the scissors the thickness of the bone between the punctures, and make this as subtle and lightly as you can, just as we said, so that you draw the bone out into your hand, or into any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and trimmed the bone, it is necessary that you take out the splinter which remains of the bone to every one other instrument resembling a scissors, but it is necessary that it be more pointed and more subtle than the other scissor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains no small bones or scales, then gently strike the bone with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with ointments and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing it, which Galen says is more suitable; and the wound becomes very firm, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the break is most open; and once you have uncovered that part, then you will place under the point of this lancet-shaped instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut at all from one side, and the part is sharp in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upwards, so that you gently strike the bone all around, and be careful of the skin that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is close to the bone, then gently strike it, because one strikes it well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate down to the skin, and the bone is struck so only above it, and there are small pieces, then you should cover that asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have various quantities of, in order to smooth them out in each place where it is most convenient, according to the operation and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you present yourself in front of coarse rasps, and then finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other delicate cut and subtle break, you should smooth it out according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily done by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, you should take a piece of linen as large as the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another piece of linen doubled in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first layer; and do this as gently as you can so that you don't irritate the skin further. Then apply another strip of linen on top and don't pull it too tight so that it only covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like this for one or two days until the swelling is reduced, then remove the dressing and administer medications such as lily roots, flax flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder of these things and apply it to the wound, and administer various universal medicines without applying any caustic.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and take care that the wound is completely clean, so that you don't leave any ointment or let it become infested with maggots, because when maggots gather above the linen of the brain, they crawl and bore, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something caustic is applied to an open sore, it becomes necrotic on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, for if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is any further blackening that comes from the medicine itself, as if it had some virtue to it, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and mix them together in a cloth, and apply it to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him with the remedies that are suitable until he is completely healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one is broken alone by itself, because these are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is crushed or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you straighten your little finger or thumb of the nose, and place this break inside your index finger, and press gently outward, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot be brought back into place with the thumb, then it is necessary that you put a small bandage or cloth on the head of a small rod, and use it to gently push the bone back into place.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in both parts, then do it again in the same way, and hasten to restore the bone to its original place as soon as possible, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If this is not possible, then after seven or ten days, when the swelling has subsided, you can attempt to straighten the nose by binding a cloth of linen to the head of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you can bind another cloth on the other side if the break is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And the restorer said that we should moisten the bandages in butter and change them every day. It doesn't seem right to me, but it's necessary that they are moistened with a mixture of almond milk, egg whites, and flour powder; then let the bandage be, as long as the bone is hard and the cartilage has firmed up.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we bind onions or goose feathers to the nose instead of bandages, and if you cover it with a soft cloth and keep the break in place, and the patient blows air through and feels some relief, then do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then I put cerot or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a small amount of aqua lum, to calm it down.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if swelling does not come to the nose, then I put an ointment on the outside, made from flour of almonds and frankincense powder, mixed with almond milk, and then apply light poultices, without binding the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break of the nose is small and it has been broken into tiny pieces, then I extract them with suitable instruments, then sew up the wound, and treat it with things that congeal and bind flesh, such as plasters and ointments suited for this, so that the bone may be reunited and the cartilage may heal.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then I treat it with bandages and put poultices on the outside until he is completely healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Here are some additional notes on the treatment of a broken jaw (mandible):
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is broken below and there is no wound on it, and the breakage is above only, and is not split in two, but rather curved inside, then one can tell by looking at it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right part, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the breakage is on the left mandible, then insert your index finger from the right hand, and push the breakage inside lightly, and pull it out with the other hand by force, and set it back in place.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the lower jaw is split in two, it is necessary that you administer traction on both sides until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the displacement of the teeth has occurred or bruising, then you should bind it with one thread of gold or silver or silk, and place over the broken jaw a cloth, and on top put a great needle well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it up so that you can see it, and command the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's condition is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what was changed, and apply a poultice over it of flour powder with plenty of egg or barley flour after you have removed the cloth; and put on top a light linen cloth, and if the poultice becomes hard and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it takes to heal; many times a healing occurs in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus forms, administer what we have said many times. (This suggests that the treatment for pus or abscess formation is to repeat a previously mentioned remedy, possibly involving applying a poultice or dressing to draw out the infection.)
