Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, repair no part of the bone that has been removed; if subtle to remove with suitable instruments for it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then you should enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on one suitable ointment to stop pus, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of great strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong forcelet breaks more than once in front, near the shoulder, and the break is either broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the most lightweight to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is like this when the break is without wound: that you have two assistants, so that one holds the aid that feels the forcelet broken; and the other stretches out the arm towards the part; then place equally the break on your hands, so that the form be such as it should be, and there be no appearance or crookedness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the patient's shoulder a round stick of cloth or linen, and let it be as thick as needed; then pull and lift up the forcelet, and hold the stick with your hand, so that you put equally the break, just as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the forcelet out because it comes from in front, it is suitable that the patient lies on his back on a mattress, and places under the shoulder a medium-sized bolster, and pushes the assistants' elbow down, so that the bone of the forcelet is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on your hands, and if it is too crowded, it is suitable that you cut in; and pull out the light pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then cut with one of the scissors that you have; but put under the forcelet this instrument to protect the flesh.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not crooked, and let it be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and have two handles, as you see them, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, just like the shape of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, it is sewn up, and if the wound is small or you doubt that there will be a hot abscess, then bandage the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms, sooth it with a poultice made of oil, rose, and vinegar, and apply it to the skin.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The splinting of the bone, when it is senseless from cuts and wounds, is that you put a poultice on the bone with flour and egg white, and put light bandages over, and if need be, place a spear under the bed to hold it in place.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage of a palm in width, then put a double drapeil over the bandages and poultice; then take a slender strip of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the strip over the break, and turn the bandage up to the collar bone, and under the healthy part of the backside, and under the ailing part; and rub each part separately, and when you see that the splint holds the break well, and you clearly see that the strip is not moving over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and have the ailing person sit with their back against something, and put a small pillow under their backside so that they can elevate the break upwards; this will alleviate the pressure on the bone by straightening out the shoulder blade, or by tying the arm to the collarbone, and do not remove it unless a bad accident occurs within twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then reapply the poultice if you see that it is needed, and let it bind and leave it as such until they are restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The break of the shoulder. It seems this text is a medical guide or recipe from medieval times, specifically dealing with setting broken bones. The language and style are consistent with Old French texts from that era.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A great deal happens when the shoulder breaks or becomes wide apart, and it is not known to be set with force except by touch; therefore it must be fixed according to the figure of the break, and rubbed according to its natural shape in all ways that you can, then put on powder of the mill with a lot of egg, and light bandages, and place on top .i. double drapeil; then place on top a wide and subtle strip, a little more than the shoulder, and if there are hairpins anywhere on the shoulder, sew them up with linen bandages so that the strip remains even, and then bind it all tightly with a large bandage so that the strip does not move from its place, and inspect the ligature every day; and each time it loosens, bind it again, and adjust the strip if it is out of place, and have the ailing person sit on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not the bone that becomes loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is protruding and pointing towards the skin, then take it up, and trim it, and do what we have said in the break of the shoulder to calm down the hot swelling. (Note: "ostee" means to cut or trim something, similar to how you would trim splinters or rough edges)
de la brisure dou pis	The break of the thigh. It seems this medieval medical guide is providing instructions for setting various types of broken bones, and now it's dealing with a more serious injury like a femur fracture (break of the thigh). The text is likely describing a complex and potentially painful process that requires careful attention to detail.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but that is rare; it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it falls downwards, and the ailing person suffers great pain, and faints easily, and perhaps vomits blood, and swells around the hairpins of the broken bone, and one knows it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient lies on their back and the physician places a cushion between the shoulders. Then they press the shoulders together, and assemble the two halves of the ribcage with their hands, subtly making them equal in all ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the affected area subtle with salt or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, securing it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the string around to the back and strain it gently. And every hour loosen the string, and if it remains loose, tighten it again. And if it is necessary to untie it due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten and untie it, and remove the plaster and treat what has come forth with the remedies of cures; then loosen the plaster and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	The breaking of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is known that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in thick areas after the back, and at the top inside, and they do not bend unless because they are slippery; and one feels it well by examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the remedy is that you put everything in place where the break is, as it should be. And then apply a plaster and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inside, the patient feels great pain and puncture, similar to that of pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and they feel sharp pains, heat and vomit a great amount of bloody fluid. This is a serious condition, and in the past, doctors have used great remedies for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And they say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break back out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make those, so hot abscesses will not come, if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the doctor look at it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said to one of us that we apply cupping glasses on the place in order to suck out the fluid, and it seems to be a good reason; nonetheless, there is doubt if the cupping glass does not bring superfluous fluids to the place because of the weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said to one of us that we should cover the place with damp wool in hot oil and put tents between the ribs so that equal warmth is given all around it, then be cured with a cure of poultice, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone which presses against the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to break up above the broken rib and it is necessary to put a certain instrument underneath to protect the spleen; and then one must saw the bone and draw it lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound if it is large, and cure with plasters until he is healed. And if hot abscesses come, then place damp cloths in rose oil on top of them, and put on the place; and cure the place from which the abscess came, and have a good physician over him where he needs to be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck (or possibly "of the break in the neck").
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	At times comes a breaking or fracture of the bone of the neck, and often it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then pay attention if you see their hands soft and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them or stretch them, and when you pinch them with a needle, if they don't feel it. Know that in many dispositions it is mortal, and if they can move and feel well when one holds and pinches them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one applies treatment there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then pay attention if the legs are softened, and if the limbs that were in the hands are gone, and there is vomiting and stooling without will on top of the back; and when one has laid him on his belly, if there is vomiting and stooling without will. And when he is laid on his back and wants to sit up, if he cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor over its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is more likely to be healed.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is hot abscess, you put oil of rose or egg yolk on the spine until it calms down; then put on a compressing and drying plaster, and bind with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is shattered, it's necessary to cover with the poultice; and take out the bone, then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it's large, with a suture, then cure with ointment unguent of animal fat until it's healed; and if the ligament of the bone is broken, which is called the "ligament of the knee", take your left hand pouch and put it in equal measure to the other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and tourniquet on it, if you need it; then tighten it, and if there's a shattered bone, do this: put it back together, and remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hipbone (or possibly "of the break in the thigh").
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Not often happens that the hipbone is broken, and if it does happen, then there is little to no diminishment to the head; and they make a long splint, and incline towards the side, and the pain comes to the patient's leg, and puncture, and swell what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand over it, as far as you can reach over the breakage; and know what kind of fracture and shape it is; and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then put the same piece back together, until it is in its natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on his belly, until you can see how to restore that breakage.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back together, then put on a plaster, then put on a splint of wood or bone, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and apply a bandage to the leg under the ribs, until the swelling is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come to it, don't touch them until the hot abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have said before; and then go back to the restoration, and bind it as needed, if there is no bad accident; and that's how it should be done.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breaking of the forearm (or possibly "of a sprain in the wrist").
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The forearm is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two manners: one of which is that you take a straight piece of wood from a willow tree of larger diameter, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two strings, and let them hang down, and instruct the patient to sit on one chair; then throw his broken arm across the handle, as far as it will reach, and place a wooden wedge in the middle of the handle, then let it hang from some heavy thing or the servants extend below; then put the bandage equally between his hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to have the patient sit on his bed, and tie his hand behind his neck; then command two servants one to stretch what is above the splint to his hands, and the other to stretch below each string, and extend both to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then tighten the string below the splint and above the splint, and have each servant extend to its part. And if the splint is close to the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to put one string in the middle under the chair, and the other towards the armpit, under the splint; and similarly if the splint is towards the armpit, it is necessary to put a lighter string slightly, without labor, until the splint is even on the arm and on the armpit; then place the splint equal as it should be, and tighten it, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if complications come, don't tighten it until 7 days, and put a warm poultice in a cloth and rose oil, until the complication is calmed; then tighten it. And the manner of tightening is that you put the splint on the splintered area, then bring the arm onto the chair, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and tighten on the chair, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, if nothing else hinders it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moved, use splints, and put on the splintered area a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two inches between each splint, and let each splint be so long that it passes over the splintered area three inches from each side; then tighten on the splints, in the same way as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the splintered area, stronger and less loosened.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see that the splints are in place and tightened as we have said, then restore the broken limb to its original position; and if you doubt the hot complication, let it be until the seventh day, as we have said; then inspect each three days the bandage, so that no itching or inflammation comes to the area, or swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow. If it does, follow what we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accident happens, then do not remove the splint until three days or more have passed, and the patient lies on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and places under the joint one cushion filled with equal amounts of wool, and watches every hour day or night that the alignment of the broken member does not move or become softened the ligaments; if it is directed by the power of medicine, and gives the patient the food we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is at its first subtlety; and when it begins to recover, it should be thick. And it is customary for the joint and leg to be re-set within 40 days of the injury; and then one must remove the splint and administer bath and ointments to guide the place back into alignment. And if the constriction is ugly and stuck, it remains to be removed in one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	The break of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small, and that is the one that touches the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is the one that is under it, towards the small joint; perhaps only the large bone breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone (foscile) is broken, the recovery is light and easy; and when the large one is broken, it is a bad healing, and more grievous than when both are broken together. If it's just the small bone that's broken, then the arm needs to be slightly stretched out and kept straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone (foscile) that's broken, then the arm needs to be strained more strongly; and stretch it out on one cushion, and tie the shoulder of the hand higher than the others, and the small joints lower than the other joints, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves, and a cushion in front of them higher than the patient's head, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then have the attendants stretch out the patient's other arm to the part under their hand, or to one ligature, and another attendant to the other side. And then place the bandages even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has several pieces, then put each one back in its place, and if any of them are dislodged, you can't get them to stay in their place, then do what we said before about using splints on either side.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is an open wound with the break, I've spoken separately about each in a special chapter; take care of it. (This suggests that the text is a medical treatise and that the author has covered various aspects of treating arm fractures and wounds in separate sections.)
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the recovery there arise suppurating abscesses, take a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, that is not too hard nor too soft; and tie it on top gently, until the abscesses are calmed down. And then remove the ointment, and apply the plaster of mill dust with abundant egg, be sure to set the stars (splints), and have the splint over the break more tight than elsewhere, and always less loosening, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths above the break be soft and moist, not hard or harsh; and let the strings, by which it is strained, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the limb and the ligature after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some evil accident comes to the member, such as pruritus (itching) that comes to the member, you should rinse the member with hot water, until those itches are calmed down; and let the member not rest too tightly. And then resume the straining, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone is dislodged, and seems like such a thing, address yourself to this remedy.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care to see that the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, then you should soften it a little bit, and let it be for some days, until the swelling goes away, and then strain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not untie them until 20 days or so, then let the patient's hands be on their neck, and let their necks be equal in length, and beware of movement and jolting, and let them sleep on their back; and know that this break is restored in 30 days or 35, and perhaps even in 20 days, according to the mixture and complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	The text appears to be a medical treatise on the treatment of arm fractures, specifically focusing on the application of bandages, splints, and other remedies to promote healing.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and near the knuckles there are many breaks, and it only rains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or swollen, it should be that the patient sits cross-legged and sits straight in front of himself also; then places his hand on the extended table, and extends the broken bones, and puts them back into place with the mirror, until they are well jointed; and applies a poultice and bandages, if a swelling comes, then he applies an splint according to the extent of the injury; and should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the loins near the belly of the palm, he makes a sphere of linen, and orders the patient to compress it against his broken palm; and then binds him with a long cloth, and should be the splint made of wood as big as the palm of the hand, and bind him, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, it should be that you put a splint above, and another one underneath in the palm, so that the hand may be open and straight, then tie up entirely around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the knuckles.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the knuckles, that is the interphalangeal joint, it should be put straight, as is necessary; and tied with the palm, and if you see fit, a small straight splint is placed to lift the break, and not move; and if the fracture is in another joint, such as the index finger or one of the others, it should be put straight, and tied with the healthy joint that comes next; or all are tied together in one bandage, whichever is better, or a splint is placed on top, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken cystone.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns in front and behind, and the restoration is such that one ties a thread or string above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each of his attendants' thread or string to an equal part, and it is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is close to the root of the hip, then it should be one of the threads towards the groin and the other threads below the breakage. And similarly if it is close to the knee, and then it should be the thread near the knee and the extension downwards; then place the splint on the bone equally in both hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and tie it, if there are any swellings, they will not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it subside then return to your work and treatment; the bandaging is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And you should wrap a strong linen bandage double-layered in two or three layers over the breakage, and let the superfluous parts remain; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and insert a long thread between the hip and the thigh, near the knee from below, and bring the ends of the thread up; then turn the bandage over the leg and the hip; put stars (splints) on top of the breakage, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the hip with soft cloth to equalize the compression; then begin to tie firmly three or four turns around the breakage; and as you go up from the breakage, the pressure will be less; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the hip, and tie three stars on top, then return to the bottom at the end of the thread, so that it reaches near the foot; and if it does not move from its place, leave it as is, without any swelling, inflammation or other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it swells again, then untie and address the swelling, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, then it is necessary to saw them off if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut through the place and draw out the splintered part; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at no time is the tendon broken when this is done to the arm and shoulder; however, in the restoration made in this way the patient does not sound.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the tendon is restored in 7 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the various constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, then it's only with a split, or an incision, i.e. a pit, and it has no wound, nor does it feel any pain, and it feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts back what was torn to its proper place, as long as it can be moved in its place, then put on the splint, and I put a rounded stake there, if you need one, and tighten it as needed, then cover all the breakages with the other bandages, just like for an abscess and similar appearance; and apply to each accident that which is fitting until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are 2 bones, of which one is called by the name "tibia" or "mustelz", and the other is called "fibula"; and it has all the same types of breaks as when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as that of the arm, and the work is just as much.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides. (This suggests a treatment where the limb is manipulated to align the bones)
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, then twist it in front. (This suggests a specific technique for realigning and stabilizing the fibula fracture)
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the thick bone (tibia) is broken, you feel great pain and you can see it well; then turn it from below. Then apply an extension, and put it back in place, and tie the bandages equally; but nevertheless, it's fitting that if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter, and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, then take two strips of fine wood that encircle the leg from one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them in two loops with a bandage above and below, and tie them together in the middle, and at this point the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some people apply one strip of wood as long as the leg, and of wood, and put the leg on to prevent movement, and properly done is what is applied in the break where there was a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; then cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and become crooked, and you have to pay attention to several dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the two bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlap each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then place your own foot over theirs, where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and bandages on top, and place a small pad under the sole of the foot two fingers deep, then bind it securely, then that you have wrapped the foot with cloth, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, you should loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they were broken, or had been dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, you should restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken toe a splint according to its length and a little thicker, then place under the foot that pad which I mentioned, and bind it securely; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, you should put over each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and bind the pad under the foot; and so long as the end of the pad is above the belly of the foot, you should press it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And be sure not to forget the other things that I have said for other fractures, which we have mentioned; and take care of each injury according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	The breaking of the bone in the joint
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's joint is broken, if she makes herself sit with her legs stretched out, then leans to the part towards the back and is held by it; then fills the natural place with cotton, and also puts as much in as one stone; then pushes the woman down and lifts up the back slowly, and then the cotton jumps so that it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, she removes the cotton, and when she has urinated, it returns to its place, and thus is done seven days or about: if the break will be restored, and you see, take a bladder of thistles, and tie a cane to the anus, and put all the bladder inside the natural place; then blow into the cane strongly, so that the bladder comes out inside: the nature will return the break; then fill with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the elbow of man is broken, or of woman, if it restores itself in this way as we have said with the hip; and these recent breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and skill into it and understands my book. For the break signifies the right path of restoration in many dispositions: hear that then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gizzard and put it inside the penis; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or about that long, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Je comprends mieux maintenant !
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be sutured now; so that the sutures that we have said will bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but it is left with vitriol scarring, and you have nothing else to do, then start again to restore the breakage at that same hour, or on that same day, before gangrene comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if gangrene comes, then leave the restoration just until the ninth day, as long as the gangrene is calmed down, and don't touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the outer layer of the skin visible, it is necessary that you put it to a light point with your hands, at an extension of little distance.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not convenient for you to put equally at your hands, then take hold of this instrument which is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and therefore it is necessary that the maker takes 3 or 4, according as he may need them for each cure of a breakage; and let it be rounded at one end, quite large, so that it does not bend with compression on the member at your work, and have an edge in front, and be thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved ends should be put on top of the visible bone; and push it in once, until it returns, and be equal one against the other. And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, as long as the instrument has control over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with a suitable instrument, such as an awl or scraper, to your power; then remove from the bone those which are remaining in it of sharpness and small scabs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. So do what you can to put it back, then moisten one cloth with black vinigrette and carefully tie it; and do not apply cerate or any other ointment on it lest it cause infection and corruption; then administer ointments as soon as the bone has been reset, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times this has happened to foolish physicians, and they have brought a fatal or corrupt condition on the patient at least once; and the constrictions are softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then do not apply ointments; but envelop around, instead of ointments, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two greenish-yellow marks appearing on the wound, then remove everything that you had put on it with vinegar, and apply a salve for healing wounds, such as tetrafarmac's ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, as long as it remains stitched and unhealed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be wrapped in such a way that the bow (or bandage) lies slightly lower than the leg.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the wound does not heal after many days and it cannot be stitched up again, but rather the bow must be reapplied, know that there are small pieces of bone within it, for which reason you should probe the wound with a tent (or a probe), and remove all these loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or other manner of corruption comes to the place (of the wound), it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in his chapter beforehand. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder bones, and others similar to the large members, do not remove it, for many times death results from this; but rather let it be until it rots; perhaps it will come out after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the swelling (or inflammation)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Bruises often come after the healing of the breakage, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the limb will not be able to perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the swelling is fresh: if the administering of stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe juice, and similar others, so that you take any one of these things or all together, and mix them with stiptic vinegar or with egg whites or with oil; and apply them to the swelling in compresses, and press it well, and do not remove it for many days; then release it, and reapply another one, as long as the nodules are removed; or you strain on a piece of linen cloth made well; for the property of the linen is that it removes all the excess fluids above the members. And if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cover it with a plaster, and let the superfluousness become apparent; or you may apply it to any poultice-maker, until it is removed, and treat it as long as it is cured.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after the member remains weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: first, because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligatures, and the swelling could not come to the member; or because of a multitude of annoyances; or because of too great movements, not at its proper hour; or because it has little blood in its body, thus it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make food for the sick person, and make the body soft, so that the blood may multiply in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and comfort. Then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great swelling, and sometimes anoint with hot water, as long as the swelling comes to the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A double member twisted after health (or wellness)
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after its restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes to great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary that they be set right with hot water, or softening herbs cooked, such as leaves of marshmallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make i.e. a mollifying plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the sap of marshmallow, and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that ease the stiffness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at no time is the bone dislocation healed by continuous and lengthy friction with moist hands. And move the member gently each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and become as hard as flint, and needs to be taken out with iron, then it is necessary to cover just up to the bone, lightly with a sharp razor, and put a compress and poultice in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it must be returned to its proper place immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if you delay, the swelling will increase, and by chance if it is set back in place with force, then it should not be moved to its proper place until it has deflated: it causes many pains and other sufferings.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	In any case, when this happens, you should heal the patient first, then let him rest until the swelling has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the limb, gently clean it, and treat each member so that each joint comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordained the chapters on dislocations up until this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Whatever happens when the jaws are dislocated in both places, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly out of their place, and a little softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the breast, and cause saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can close his mouth, and enwrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place by itself within a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully developed, you must clean it immediately, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in this way the servants should hold the patient's head, and insert a mirror on a stick into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if it is two-thirds deep; and with one hand, place it in the middle, and with the other two hands be outside to balance it; and command the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror should be placed in a straight line with it, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return them to place, or if they are both jaws together, then warm water and oil should be applied to them, until they are lightly cleaned; and do not delay the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they have been returned to their place and the patient's mouth closes well without much effort, then apply a warm compress made of rose oil and beeswax on top of it, and tie it loosely with linen threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on their back, and their dogs (i.e. hands) placed between two pillows, so that they do not move them to the right or left, nor make any effort to eat, but take light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws have healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he may take what he wants lightly, and not strain himself to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jaws have completely healed and are sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be returned to their place within an hour and are not converted back to their natural position, then fever and chills set in, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of pure yellow bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a perilous condition; and many times death comes to the person who experiences it within eight days.
de la forcelle	the jaw joint (literally "of the forceps", but in medical context referring to the mandible or jawbone)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The joint (of the mandible) cannot be dislocated from the side towards the front (i.e. into the mouth), and it can only be dislocated once towards the back, and that is when you know it has happened.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on their back, and extends their arms; and then presses firmly with your palm to the dislocated joint, and it will return; then apply a poultice and bandage to it, and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the hand that is on the outside (i.e. the side) cannot be dislocated; if it were to come out at all, then clean and put it back in its place, as we have said before; then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly, and command the patient to rest until they are fully healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly, the hand is brought back from the side, when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder joint dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one of which is when it comes out from under the collarbone (acromion); and the second is when it comes out from the front (anteriorly); and possibly it comes out upwards, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate backwards from the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward towards the chest; but rather it dislocates downwards under the collarbone, and this happens most often in people with little fat, because then it slips out easily; in those who have enough fat, it slips out slowly and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they have an inflammation or swelling of the shoulder, and the shoulder is swollen with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you should probe into it, until you are certain, and once you are sure, then start the treatment.
