Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when the shoulder goes downwards towards the collarbone, and you will find a clear distinction between the healthy and diseased shoulders, and you will see a manifest difference.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and under the collarbone, at the point where the arm meets the body, just like an empty nest; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their side, nor make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, then it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the point where the arm meets the body.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this way of dislocating is not to be reduced (i.e. restored to its original position) when it is new or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister raises the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the collarbone, and raises the jointure with force upwards to its place; and the minister raises the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back down, and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come back as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the minister should gently and soothingly apply a compress, such as a decoction of alecost, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and bring it to the place.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	and then the patient should be covered on their back, and a strip of linen of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the collarbone; then the minister should place their elbow on top of the strip, and gently lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another minister should grasp the patient's head, so that it does not move down; and the shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see that it is restored to its place in this way, then know.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you should have a man present who is larger than the patient, and stand with their shoulder against the patient's back, and push the collarbone up high, so that the patient hangs from the arm.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister should pull the patient's hand downwards towards their belly. And if the patient is too lightweight, they can hang something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also healed in another way: and that is by sticking a long spit into the ground, whose end is as thick as a fist, and not too big or too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and then it is placed under the patient, but in such a way that it is covered with a soft cloth on top, and the patient's hand is stretched out to the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return after all the things we have said, then do this cure: take a spit of two arm-lengths and three fingers' width in diameter, which has the end rounded so that it can easily enter into depth under the collarbone, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	and tie a cloth on top of the spit so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it under the patient's collarbone; and stretch out your arm over the long spit, and tie the elbow to the spit, and the arm at the hand, then put the arm on a cushion of a wooden board, one finger's width thick, and have the hands hanging down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will come back immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And once it is healed, in whatever way it may be, then you should place under the collarbone a ball of wool of equal thickness; and apply an ointment made from flour powder with incense and egg yolks all over the shoulder and around it; and bind the bandage under the collarbone gently, and turn the cloth back on the ointment, and wrap the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he rest a little while, until the members are comforted, because it will heal more quickly; and then let him rest some more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because it has been moistened or for some other reason, then you should apply cauteries to three punctures, such as those used on the front or back of a cautery stick.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and the dislocation happens again after seven days, and the joint does not hold and the arm cannot be lifted upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs towards the chest or breasts or back is caused by a blow or stretching of the hands, and it requires another type of treatment. And one must treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the member and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until the swelling is alleviated and the member returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in various ways and returns to its place in the same way, whether it was dislocated in front or behind, and the dislocation is not restored, because one can see it well and feel it well; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the diseased shoulder to the healthy one, it will be quite apparent. Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor can it touch its own shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to treat it so that hot abscesses do not form, because if hot abscesses do form, it will be painful to reduce it; and by chance it cannot be completely reduced, especially when it occurs in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death can occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is this: when it can be reduced to such an extent that one can bring it back into place, then you should extend its hand with both of yours; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands of the minister should follow the shoulder around, on top and underneath, and push the joint into its hollow or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will come back when it doubles its hand over its own hand, and presses the root of the palm against the shoulder that was dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and have two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with both of their hands, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, and while you are wrapping a double long and wide cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the minister has joined the joint to their hand, they should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, and then push the joint firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is back in its place, then apply a dry ointment with egg yolk on top of the joint, and bind it firmly, and let the arm rest against the patient's neck for some days, and then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the ointment and the bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set, and then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels swollen after the joint has been put back in place, and it stiffens, then bathe it and rub it gently, and press on it until it is soothed; or you can apply a poultice made from fat sheep's wool to the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and let it go into a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it sweats, then rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then go into a bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you see fit, apply a compress made from moistened cow's hair that has been heated with butter, and bind it to the joint, and it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and it is a light return, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back into place quickly, even if it is swollen or if a hot abscess forms in it.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is that you place the diseased hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and the minister should place it evenly, so that his palm is over the appearance of the joint, and push it back into place until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, it is necessary to check if it is properly in place; then have the patient place their back of hand on a table at extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then have the patient place their back of hand on a table, and the minister should put their hand over the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply a soothing plaster to the abscess and let it be so without reattempting the reduction.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and it does no harm to the patient until such time as the hand is softened and cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries are damaged; if there is no other reason for this than to use a cautery near the case, and by chance it is not worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is back in place, then apply the ointment that we have said, and bind it and let it be for five days, then release it and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some swelling, then bathe the hand in warm water, and rub it gently until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At any time, the fingers of the hand can become dislocated on either side, or towards the back of the palm or towards the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then extend the finger and push the dislocation back into place with your fingers, then hold the tip of the finger and gently bend it towards the joint.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it be for two days, and then put it back in its place that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and release it every day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this often, until it is straight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated towards the belly of the hand, and do what you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same thing when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the hip bone (ischium) at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip bone (ischium) at the back or near the tailbone is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, because death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the patient's bowels jump out without volition, and they cannot be held in, and multiple members become softened, such as the two thighs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the hip bone moves to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "giltbiositez".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to reduce it, if the giltbiositez has come since childhood; if not, there will be no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment by great words say it has no true benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the giltbiositez that occurs at the front of the chest, there is no cause or cure.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and similarly that which occurs directly in both sides, and one cannot cure it except for the proper one that occurs at the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched out on their face in one place evenly, and have a bandage underneath them so that they are not hurt.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert a burning stick at the head into the earth firmly, and another at the feet, and bind a bandage around the patient's shoulders, and hips, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two ministers should hold the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two burning sticks.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be well closed, the burning sticks as we have said, and the minister should put their palms on the spine firmly until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a wooden board of three arms in length, and hollow out the underside, and have the patient lie on their side, and insert the head of the board into the hollowed-out part, then place the middle of the board over the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and set the mirrors under his feet on the other side of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do so in the turning that turns back to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And then you place two torches at the head of the patient on one arm, and near the feet two others, with about an inch in between each torch.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and on each torch have one perforation, where the turning pole goes through, and let the torches be firmly in the earth, so that they do not move; and between each two torches have a turning pole, on which the patient turns, and on each turning pole have two small torches an inch long, to turn the patient.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is between the straps to the turning pole towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other turning pole, and each of the servants turn their poles until all the cords are taut, and the master sets the needle in place just as we said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, he places on top a desiccating plaster with an abundance of egg yolk, and then the bandages, and then the needle of a piece three inches long, which pierces the place of the gallbladder and the healthy part of the spleen, then ties it with a cord, as we have said, and uses the patient for subtle nourishment, until they are cured.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if nothing comes to an end in the health, it is necessary to administer soothing and mollifying medicines with the needle that we have said before; and at no time should one administer more than one piece of cloth.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and at any time the appearance appears in the back part of the spine, and it seems like dislocation; and it's the bone that is splitting open, so one should not have any presumptions about it, for fear that death might come from it.
des dislocations de la hainche	It looks like we've reached a new section of text.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that dislocations occur only in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, but not so in other joints; and the joint of the hip is displaced according to four parts: inward and outward, front and back; and more inward, and it comes undone before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	The knowledge of the dislocation is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee joint opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee at the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place that is next to an inflamed and hot pustule, because the veins of the groin go there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes on the outside is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him whose it comes on the inside is that he can move his leg well according to its completion; however, do not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go, he cannot walk forward, holds back his urine, swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him whose it comes behind is that he cannot spread his knee joint, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the groin are at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation is that you return to see if the dislocation was ancient and has remained according to its position, in which case there is no cure; and it is not necessary to have any hope.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, you should hurry to return the joint to its proper place, inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, you should have one skilled servant bring the leg forcefully and hold it tightly with both hands, or with one strap tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another servant extends his hand above in such a manner that he presses his hands against the patient's hips, then tightens with one soft strap on the groin; and another ties the end of the strap.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch both ends at once, as far as is necessary, until the patient is lifted off the ground and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, it is necessary to apply treatment to its resemblance. When the dislocation is at the back of the knee, you should take a splint and place it on the healthy side of the patient's leg, then tie the strap over the root of the groin, and the part that is under the anger, then tighten the strap upwards towards the angle, and the strong part.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take hold of another servant's arms and encircle the swollen part of the patient's groin, and stretch it outwards strongly: if it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this way as we have said, it is necessary that you tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft strap on both heels and ankles, and the sick leg be stretched out two inches more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then it should be suspended from the top of a beam and be above the ground two feet long; then command one servant to encircle the head of the groin, and have another servant hang with the patient, who tightly encircles the groin, for the jointure returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the front, have the patient lie down as we said in the case of the swelling, and tighten one strap on the sick leg properly, and also on the thigh.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two hot irons, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one of them between the groin bones of the patient in the form of a cross.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have the wet cloths wrapped around them to prevent scalding the patient, then have each servant stretch towards him and the physician place the hot iron on the patient's hand with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, put him on the table and press him as we have said in the procedure for a dislocation of the shoulder blade, and place the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be stretched hastily and according to what I have said; and place the mirror on the patient's pain above the sick joint, then press with the other hand and stretch it down towards the elbow.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it must not be stretched down or lifted up on the earth, but rather that he should be as if the hip were dislocated to the back, as we have said for laying on two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on his face, and the band should be stretched as we have said above, and he must be pressed on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be done when the patient stretches his legs and they are equal; then join the thighs together, put the splint and the strain of a bandage on it, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and let him rest for 3 or 4 days, then remove it and put the splint on; and if you see that they are equal, add the strain as before, and leave it for 3 days; then remove it and make him walk gently, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	On the dislocation of the elbow.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and do not become dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if it does not return to its place at their knee, know that they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight, and stretch their leg if they can, and put your back on their face, and place their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee to your palms and draw it between your two hands, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply; and another assistant stretches their foot so that the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that they will have bent their leg at their knee lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the plaster on it, and make their leg return to its place at the knee, and bind them together strongly for three days or four, then let them go; and do not let the patient walk until the members are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the member is not well, then administer stretching strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like a new topic!
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated within and behind.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is inflamed, and tense before the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return to its place is slight, and you must stretch it slightly with your hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you should have the sick person sit upright, and put a splint i.e. a support except by the leg, over the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left .two times, then stretch it up high, and push the foot firmly up high;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this .two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back, that's well; if not, then start over again with the work, for it will come back;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot come back like this, then have the sick person lie on their back on the ground, and place .one sturdy support firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloth around to prevent them from hurting themselves;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then bind the support to the thigh, and another support extend the foot to his hands or to .one cord, so that he ties it above the ankle joint.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each support equally, and the cords should be placed tight between the thighs of the sick person to hold the sick person in place when you stretch it.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the skilled person take hold of the dislocation at their hands, and another support binds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it's back in place, you should apply the poultice and bandage on top, and form the splint, and bind the foot to the leg, and take care that the strips above the ankle behind are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then leave it for .two or .three days, and if the bandages loosen, then rewrap the splint. Then remove it on the third day or quarter of that time, and prevent the sick person from walking for .four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if they walk before this term ends, it is not certain that it will not relapse again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus or swelling comes up, you should reduce it, as we have said elsewhere, until they are completely healed.
des dois	It looks like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! "De dislocatione pedis" (On dislocation of the foot) seems to be a brief guide for treating a specific type of injury or condition. If you'd like, I can try to summarize what we've learned from it.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated (or sore), they should be gently stretched without effort, and that's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in front of the ankle joint of the foot, you should have the sick person sit on .one plain or flat surface or on .the table right out, and put your foot over what appears to be the joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it's equal and there's nothing apparent, place under the sole of the foot a board on two legs, then form the splint, and leave it for .three days, then remove it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It looks like we're switching to a new section of the text, which deals with treating wounds and dislocations together! This might be an interesting combination of injury types, as both wounds and dislocations require different approaches to healing. If you'd like, I can try to summarize what we've learned so far from this medieval medical text.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not cautious in the treatment, if you're not skilled in the art and haven't used it for a long time, and if you're not patient, merciful, and slow, but rather bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use gentle soothing remedies at the beginning, and leave the sick person in God's hands if you don't see any hope of healing.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see some hope, then clean and cleanse the member now at leisure, so that the hot swelling may come. (This suggests that once there's a chance for healing, it's time to take more active steps in treating the wound or dislocation.)
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is clean, then administer soothing remedies for the hot swelling, and treat the wound with drying ointments, as it seems fitting.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is breakage and small bones are broken, then set them, and do what we have said about simple diseases (i.e., treat the resulting wound or injury).
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and beware of falling into a path of fear, as I have said, for this is worth more to you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom that will arm and protect your soul and body. Amen. (This final sentence seems to be a message from the author, encouraging the reader to approach their work with courage and faith.)
Explicit le romen de fisique	It looks like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! "Explicit" is Latin for "ends here", and "le romen de fisique" means "the book on physics" or more likely, "the book of surgery".
